1934.11.07

Today's Main Points of This Newspaper

Domestic: The Executive Yuan decided to appoint Liu Weichi as Political Vice Minister of the Ministry of Industries and Gu Zhenggang as Permanent Vice Minister; the Guangdong bandit suppression army captured Chengkou; Jiang toured Yungang.

Foreign: Britain is striving to mediate the deadlock in the Naval Reduction Conference; the French Parliament opened, and the fate of the cabinet is hanging by a thread.

Shanghai: Chinese tobacco merchants requested the cancellation of the Shaanxi tobacco surtax; Mao Yisheng talked about the definite date for the commencement of the Qiantang River Bridge.

Chengkou Has Been Reported Recovered

No Bandit Traces Within Renhua

[Hong Kong] Shaoguan, 6th: Chen Hankuang's brigade captured Chengkou on the 5th. At the same time, the bandits besieging Changjiangxu also retreated. There are no bandit traces within Renhua County. (6th Special Dispatch)

[Changsha] The bandits who attacked Rucheng were defeated by the [□□□] brigade and fled towards Renhua on the Guangdong border. The Guangdong army is intercepting them. (6th Special Dispatch)

[Chongqing] A part of He's bandits, about two to three thousand people, raided Youyang County. They were repelled by the Sichuan army. The Hunan army's [□□] brigade is pursuing He's bandits and has entered [□□] County. (6th Special Dispatch)

[Changsha] He Jian reported in his memorial week speech on the 5th that the bandit 13589th Corps fled west and arrived at Rucheng on the 2nd. The battle lasted until the late afternoon of the 4th, killing hundreds of bandits. The Guangdong army is following in pursuit, and it is hoped that they will be exterminated. He hopes that the entire province will remain calm and pay all due fees, assist in transportation, and provide provisions and corvée labor, and to raise the courage to suppress the bandits. (6th Special Dispatch)

Ninghua Will Be Recovered Soon

[Xiamen] According to military news, the city of Ninghua can be recovered within one or two days. Only a small number of local communists remain in the cities of Ninghua and Qingliu, which is not a problem. (6th Special Dispatch)

The Authorities Decided to Raise a Large Sum to Relieve Refugees in Changting

[Fuzhou] The Jiangxi Xingying telegram to the Eastern Route Army commends the recapture of Changting. The remnant bandits who fled from Tingxi were pursued by the National Army near Gucheng on the 3rd, killing more than 700 bandits and wounding hundreds. Because they could not keep up, many threw themselves into the river and committed suicide. The authorities, considering that Changting has suffered from banditry for a long time and the people are in deep distress, decided to raise a large sum to relieve the refugees and provide free transportation for refugees from Changting scattered in various places to return to their hometowns. (5th Special Dispatch)

[Xiamen] Zhangzhou telegram: After Changting was recovered on the 1st, the commander of the 4th Column, Li Yannian, immediately entered the city to appease the people. The people welcomed him along the way. Ding Guobao, director of the Political Training Office, convened a mass meeting of the people, attended by more than 4,000 people, and elected five local gentry to form a temporary town office to work with the military and political authorities to determine prices and handle all post-disaster affairs. At the same time, administrative officials were instructed to investigate household registrations and organize baojia. People who had been coerced into joining the bandits and who repented and started anew came one after another. Farmers who had fled to various places outside, carrying hoes and plows, followed the army to return to their hometowns in an endless stream. (6th Central News Agency Telegram)

Jiang Visited Yungang

[Beiping] Jiang went to Yungang for sightseeing in a car under strict guard at 4 pm yesterday. He continued sightseeing this morning. (6th Special Dispatch)

[Beiping] Princes Yun and De have rushed to Guihua from Bailing Temple. (6th Special Dispatch)

[Beiping] Qian Zongze left Beiping with Jiang for Zhangjiakou on the 3rd and returned from Zhangjiakou yesterday. He arrived in Beiping this morning. (6th Special Dispatch)

[Taiyuan] Zhangjia arrived in Taiyuan from Taiyuan on the evening of the 6th. (6th Special Dispatch)

Kong Xiangxi Rescheduled His Flight to Beiping for Today

[Nanjing] Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi originally planned to fly to Beiping in his own Continetal airplane on the 6th, but because the plane did not arrive in Nanjing in time, and because he still had to attend the Central Political Conference on the morning of the 7th to make a report, he rescheduled his departure to the afternoon of the 7th. (6th Special Dispatch)

[Beiping] The parties concerned here received a telegram from Kong Xiangxi in Nanjing saying that he had originally planned to come to Beiping on the morning of the 6th, but had to stay in Nanjing for business and rescheduled his flight north for the morning of the 8th. Please inform all parties. (6th Special Dispatch)

Bandit Atmosphere in Zunhua and Yutian Areas Is Still Dangerous

[Tianjin] In the Jieshankou and Yanshankou areas of Zunhua, bandits once again dispersed into smaller groups on the 4th and harassed at night, constantly attacking the defenses of the people's corps. Gunfire was incessant all night. The Zunhua County Magistrate ordered each district and each fort on the 5th to provide 20 men per fort and 100 men per district to strengthen the defenses of each pass. (6th Special Dispatch)

[Tianjin] The waters of the Huanxiang River and Shuangcheng River in Yutian have risen, and the banks have overflowed, creating a vast expanse of water. Recently, more than a dozen bandit boats suddenly appeared in the river. Taking advantage of the lack of guards in the river, they docked along the river and robbed villages. On the night of the 3rd, the Mi Yingpu Village was invaded by ten bandit boats, which looted for three hours, tied up their loot, and fled. The people in the vicinity had nowhere to report. Recently, dozens of villages jointly petitioned the county government to quickly prepare river defenses. In Shuigu Town, Jichang County, 180 bandits with rifles were discovered on the 4th, looting the entire town. Villagers fled in droves. More than 300 members of the Tang County and Jichang County People's Corps and police defenses had joined forces and rushed to suppress them on the night of the 4th. (6th Special Dispatch)

[Tianjin] On the night of the 5th, a large group of more than 90 bandits was discovered in Guozhuangzi, Yutian, occupying the village and refusing to leave. All the villages in the vicinity were looted. The local people's corps in the county were transferred out, leaving no troops to suppress them. At about 3 am this morning, more than a dozen thieves were discovered in the Haihe River in Tianjin. They boarded a cargo ship at Wharf No. 4 of the China Merchants Bureau in the British Concession and robbed it, searching and seizing for an hour before disembarking and fleeing. Security on the Haihe River has therefore been tightened today. (6th Special Dispatch)

Iron Sand Ore Found in Majiagou Mine

[Tianjin] Iron sand ore has also been discovered in the Dongbaidaozi Mountain of the Kailuan Majiagou Mine. The ore vein is deeply buried three feet underground and the area is wider than that of Tangjiazhuang, about nearly 30 square miles. Recently, 32 local residents raised funds to mine it, and can produce hundreds of tons per day. Each ton is sold to Tangshan Qixin Cement Company for 3.2 yuan per ton. However, this iron sand contains less iron and is not as good as that of Tangjiazhuang. (6th Special Dispatch)

Japanese Control of Mining Industry Throughout Northeast China

[Beiping] News from outside the Pass: In order to control the mining industry throughout Northeast China, Japan has decided to centralize the mining affairs of various provinces and decided to establish four mining supervision offices, abolish the mining affairs sections of the industrial departments of various provinces, and the directors of the four offices are all Japanese, located in Shenyang, Changchun, Longjiang, and Chengde. (6th Special Dispatch)

Executive Yuan Decided to Establish Central Rural Service Training Institute

Approved candidates for Political and Administrative Vice Ministers

[Nanjing] The Executive Yuan held its 185th meeting at 9 am on the 6th. Wang Zhaoming, He Yingqin, Kong Xiangxi, Wang Shijie, Chen Gongbo, Shi Qingyang, Chen Shuren, Chen Shaokuan, Huang Shaoxiong, Liu Ruiheng, and Zhu Jiahua attended. Chairman Wang Zhaoming decided on the following important cases:

A. Resolutions on appointments and removals: (1) Guo Chuntao, Political Vice Minister of the Ministry of Industries, reported that the scope of industrial investigation was too broad and requested approval to resign from his position as Political Vice Minister. This was approved. The vacancy was filled by the transfer of Liu Weichi, Permanent Vice Minister of the Ministry of Industries. The vacant position of Permanent Vice Minister was filled by Gu Zhenggang. (2) Chairman Han of the Shandong Provincial Government reported that Weng Zhiquan, secretary and section chief of the Finance Department of the provincial government, requested to resign from his concurrent position as section chief. It is proposed that Yu Baosheng be appointed to fill the vacancy. Approved. (3) Chairman Lu of the Zhejiang Provincial Government reported that He Yanglie, secretary of the provincial government, has been appointed to another position. It is proposed that Gu Shou be appointed to fill the vacancy. Approved. (4) Minister He of the Ministry of Military Administration reported that he requested the appointment of Qin Shifan as a major general instructor of military science at the Army University. Approved. (5) Minister He of the Ministry of Military Administration reported that he requested the appointment of Yang Zhenguang as the commander of the 474th Regiment of the 237th Brigade of the 79th Division. Approved.

B. Discussion and resolutions: (1) Minister Wang of the Ministry of Education reported that the Mingxian Middle School, a private school in Shanxi Province, has achieved remarkable results in its management. Recently, it plans to expand agricultural and industrial subjects to cultivate students' labor production capacity, which is also essential. It is proposed to allocate 30,000 yuan from the first reserve fund of the national education and culture fund this year to provide subsidies. Approved. (2) Minister Gu of the Ministry of Railways reported that all ticket price reductions and exemptions, special passes, and accounting carriages for the Qingping through train are not applicable. Please approve and forward this to the National Government for promulgation and compliance, and send a letter to the Central Political Conference for record and notify all relevant parties. Approved. (3) Minister Chen of the Ministry of Industries reported that the Shanghai, Beijing, Guangdong, Pingjin, Zhejiang, Hankou, and Shandong Accountants' Associations jointly reported that the current Accountants Ordinance has been found to be difficult to fully comply with the legislative intent in practice. A written explanation is attached, requesting revision and implementation. The original explanation is enclosed, and opinions are added, requesting verification and transfer to the Legislative Yuan for consideration and revision. Consult the Legislative Yuan. (4) The Central Antiquities Preservation Committee submitted the proposed meeting rules and detailed rules of procedure of the committee for verification and implementation. Approved with amendments. (5) Chairman Chen of the Jiangsu Provincial Government submitted the revised method for reporting urban land prices in Jiangsu Province for verification and compliance. Approved. (6) The National Government ordered that the General Accounting Office submit the proposed general budget for national ordinary revenue and expenditure for the 23rd year, as well as various attachments and the Central Political Conference, to revise the national ordinary general budget for the 23rd year. Please issue an order to the Executive Yuan to submit it to the Legislative Yuan for review and promulgation and implementation. Ordered to comply accordingly. (7) Minister He of the Ministry of Military Administration submitted the rank table of soldiers of the army, navy, and air force for verification and referral to the public. Approved. (8) It was decided to establish a Central Rural Service Training Institute, and the plan and budget were submitted to the Central Political Conference. (6th Central News Agency Telegram)

[Nanjing] The Central Rural Service Training Institute, which was approved to be established by the Executive Yuan, is expected to enroll 200 to 300 students in each session. Graduates of universities are qualified. The site is decided to be in Nanjing. Professors are planned to be hired from various universities and experts in Nanjing. Each training session lasts for half a year, and then they are assigned to various experimental counties for one year of practice. (6th Special Dispatch)

[Nanjing] Free tickets and credit methods are not applicable to the Youth Through Train. The resolution was passed by the Executive Yuan on the 6th and submitted to the National Government and the Central Political Conference for promulgation and compliance. The Ministry of Railways also decided on the operating methods of the through train and issued an order to all lines to comply. The content is as follows: (1) Attach the through train and stipulate that it will run once a week in each direction. (2) The Jiaoji Railway will prepare one first-class and second-class sleeping car for attachment. (3) The operating period is from April 1st to September 30th each year. (4) Every Tuesday, it will be attached from Qingdao to Jinan, and then transferred to the Shanghai-Beiping through train to Beiping. Every Friday, it will be attached from Beiping to the Shanghai-Beiping through train to Jinan, and then transferred to Qingdao. (6th Central News Agency Telegram)

Ministry of Judicial Administration Held Departmental Meeting Yesterday

[Nanjing] The Ministry of Judicial Administration held a departmental meeting in the afternoon of the 6th. Ju Zheng presided over the meeting. Both Vice Ministers Xie and Pan and all directors and section chiefs attended. First, the directors reported on the recent situation of their respective departments and expressed their opinions on what should be promoted and what should be reformed. (6th Special Dispatch)

[Nanjing] The Ministry of Judicial Administration issued an order on the 6th to appoint Song Shuqiao as acting secretary of the ministry with the rank of Simplified Appointment, Miao Hongjun as acting section chief of the ministry, and Zhang Jiuwei as a member of the Judicial Official Qualification Review Committee. In addition, Guan Ji, director of the General Affairs Department, is to be removed from his position pending another appointment. (6th Special Dispatch)

Tao Shangming Went to Tangshan to Handle Affairs of the Commissioner's Office

[Beiping] Tao Shangming went to Tianjin this afternoon and then to Tangshan to handle the affairs of the Commissioner's Office and to schedule a meeting of the county magistrates of the Luanyu District to discuss rectifying officialdom and implementing winter defense in various counties. (6th Special Dispatch)

[Tianjin] Tao Shangming has returned to Tangshan. The discussion meeting on administrative diplomacy and security of the county magistrates of the Luanyu District, which was originally scheduled to be held on the 8th, has been changed to the 10th because of insufficient time to prepare. He Xiaoyi, the magistrate of Zunhua County in the Jiji District, was invited to attend. (6th Special Dispatch)

Central Government Sends Personnel to Investigate Bones of Soldiers Who Resisted Japan

[Tianjin] The bones of the soldiers of Hebei Province who died in the battle against Japan on the Great Wall line were investigated by Cai Liangbi, Liu Baoqin, and other four investigation committee members sent by the Central Government to various battlefields. More than 11,000 bones have been found. Two bones from every 200 will be selected as the main and deputy loyal remains and transported to the Zijin Mountain Cemetery in Nanjing for burial. Cai and others arrived in Shijiazhuang on the 5th and will transfer to Jin Sui for investigation. (6th Special Dispatch)

Liu Zhi Finished Physical Examination in Beiping

[Beiping] Liu Zhi stayed in Union Hospital for a physical examination a few days ago, which has now been completed. There are no diseases. After resting for two or three more days, he can be discharged from the hospital and return to Henan. (6th Special Dispatch)

Ministry of Industries Issued License to Jinbei Mining Bureau

[Nanjing] Yan Xishan and others developed the coal mine in Jinbei and engaged in the affiliated businesses related to the mining industry in Jinbei, raising 1.5 million yuan. The Jinbei Mining Bureau Renfen Co., Ltd. was organized in Datong County, Shanxi Province, and applied to the Ministry of Industries for registration and registration. The list of directors included Yan Baichuan, Liang Ruzhou, Liang Shangtong, Geng Buzhan, Qiu Yangjun, Fan Xiangli, and supervisors Sun Nanbin and Li Shanggu. The Ministry of Industries has approved the registration and issued a license yesterday. (6th Special Dispatch)

It Is Said That Treasures in Yi Peiji's Hands Were Demanded by the Puppet Regime

[Tianjin] Yi Peiji is hiding in the Japanese Concession on Naniwa Street in Tianjin and is very unfree. Gangsters and ruffians extort him every day. Zheng Xiaoxu believes that the treasures of the Qing Dynasty should belong to the Qing Dynasty, and sent Kishida, a Japanese official of the puppet State Council, to Tianjin to demand most of the treasures from Yi Peiji. Yi is therefore extremely annoyed and resentful. (6th Special Dispatch)

After the Start of the Huai River Project, Civilians Enlisted Actively

[Nanjing] According to the Huai River Guidance Association, after the groundbreaking ceremony in Qingjiangpu, civilian laborers began to be recruited. In less than a month, 160,000 civilian laborers have been recruited. All the required equipment is provided by the civilians themselves. The cost savings are significant, which shows that the people of Jiangsu have a deep understanding of the benefits of the Huai River project. The project is now divided into seven sections, with one engineer assigned to each section to be responsible for guidance and supervision. Ge Jilou is the chief engineer and is responsible for the overall project and plan. (6th Special Dispatch)

[Qingjiangpu] Recently, Huai River workers have been stationed in towns along the abandoned Yellow River. Among them, there are more in Lianshui County, and the rest are a thousand or hundreds. The business of various food shops is excellent, and the price of firewood and rice has also risen slightly, which is different from the past when supply exceeded demand. (6th Special Dispatch)

Japanese Emperor's Sister Arrived in Beiping

[Beiping] Princess Akiko, the sister of the Japanese Emperor Showa, and seven or eight attendants arrived in Beiping by train from Tianjin this morning. After getting off the train, they went to the Fusang Hall to stay. (6th Special Dispatch)

Strong Wind and Sudden Cold in Beiping

[Beiping] There was a strong wind and sudden cold in Beiping all day today, and it has frozen. (6th Special Dispatch)

Bandits Discovered in Baotou

[Beiping] News from Baotou: More than 200 bandits who fled from Wu, led by Fu Baochang and Chang Ziyi, have now fled to the Zhao Dahuan area. Regiment Commander Li of the cavalry regiment ordered the 3rd and 4th companies of the regiment to rush to Lianshan Naobao to pursue and suppress them. The 1st and 2nd companies of the regiment are currently pursuing and suppressing the Liang bandits and have entered the territory of Wuchuan. (6th Special Dispatch)

Reservoir to Be Built in the Upper Reaches of the Yongding River

[Beiping] A reservoir will be built in Huailai in the upper reaches of the Yongding River, and construction is scheduled to begin next spring. (6th Special Dispatch)

Panchen Lama Will Go to Gansu to Propagate

[Beiping] The Panchen Lama has changed his plan to return to Tibet in the summer of next year and will go to Gansu and Ximeng to propagate recently. (6th Special Dispatch)

Second Phase of Heavy Taxes and Levies in Hebei Province Completed

[Beiping] The Hebei Department of Finance has completed the abolition of the second phase of heavy taxes and levies in the province and has issued an order to all counties that, unless there are special circumstances and those not related to government construction, they can be abolished in accordance with the seven principles set by the Ministry and completed by the end of the year. (6th Special Dispatch)

Luan Dong White Flour Sales Are Very Smooth

The Japanese and Korean ronin drug agencies in various places in Luan Dong refine white flour into yellow flour and sell it very well. Recently, there are three fake manufacturing agencies in Tangshan, Qinhuangdao, and Changli, manufacturing day and night, and being trafficked by traitors. (6th Special Dispatch)

Flower Associations Are Prevalent in Kailuan Mines

[Tianjin] Flower associations are prevalent in Kailuan mines, and gambling dens are everywhere. In Linxi alone, there are two flower associations and more than 20 gambling dens. The flower associations are held twice a day, morning and evening, and each time the winnings and losses are about 3,000 yuan. The staff in the association monitor with guns and ignore the law. At this time of local desolation and winter defense, it has a great impact on public security. As for the drug scourge in Tangshan, since the establishment of the anti-smoking institute, the investigation and prohibition of smokers has been very strict. Many Japanese and Korean companies have suffered losses and closed down, and the white flour business has gradually become deserted. According to a recent survey, there are currently only 164 foreign companies in Tangshan, a decrease of more than 60 compared to last year. (6th Central News Agency Telegram)

Jinan Financial Situation Gradually Stabilizing

[Jinan] A few days ago, unscrupulous merchants smuggled cash to Dalian for profit. The city's cash suddenly decreased from 6 million yuan to 2 million yuan. Now the Department of Finance prohibits the export of cash, and the Bank of Communications and the Central Bank have transported cash to the city. The city now has more than 5 million yuan, and the financial situation has stabilized. (6th Special Dispatch)

Shandong Province Preparing to Establish Local Tax Bureau

[Jinan] The Department of Finance is preparing to establish local tax bureaus in various counties in accordance with the Ministry's order and plans to levy taxes in five grades. (6th Special Dispatch)

Japanese Envoy Arima Passed Through Jinan to Beiping

[Jinan] Arima passed through Jinan to Beiping for talks today and will return to Jinan via Qingdao next week. (6th Special Dispatch)

Director of Shandong-Henan Unified Tax Bureau Assumed Office

[Qingdao] The newly appointed Director of the Shandong-Henan Unified Tax Bureau, Tang Xiang, arrived in Qingdao from Nanjing on the 5th and took office on the afternoon of the 6th. (6th Special Dispatch)

Shen Honglie Convened Subordinates to Speak

[Qingdao] Shen Honglie convened subordinates to speak for several days. On the 5th, it was the heads of various bureaus and stations; on the 6th, it was the section chiefs; on the 7th, it was the heads of rural district construction, urging them to be diligent, prudent, and public-spirited, and to be honest and self-disciplined. Shen will go to Hubei in the middle of the month to bury his parents. (6th Special Dispatch)

National Examination and Selection Conference Declaration

Government to Oversee University Graduation Exams

Examination and Appointment Sub-Offices to Be Established in Each Province

Provisional Plan for Civil Servant Protection Agreed Upon

[Nanjing] Full text of the declaration of the National Examination and Selection Conference: The Examination Yuan of the National Government convened the National Examination and Selection Conference in the capital on November 1, 1934. Representatives from central government agencies and various provinces, municipalities, and counties, as well as representatives and experts from national universities and independent colleges, attended. There were 160 attendees and 38 observers. A total of 95 proposals were discussed. The conference lasted five days and concluded successfully. A brief overview is presented here to inform the nation. Today, the Chinese people have two major aspirations: first, a clean and honest government; and second, national progress. To achieve progress in governance, it is essential to have definite standards for the promotion and demotion of civil servants. To achieve national progress, all talented individuals must have the opportunity to serve. To address both, it is imperative to select true talent through examinations and prevent opportunistic advancements through proper appointment procedures. This ensures that capable individuals hold positions without the mindset of a short-term appointment, and that competent individuals can achieve tangible results within three years. To achieve these goals, we have agreed on several practical measures. Let us first discuss the examination aspect. The state's selection of talent must originate from schools. The subjects tested should align with the educational level of the schools. In the future, the subjects and level of both general and higher-level exams should closely align with the curriculum standards or subject outlines set by the Ministry of Education. Furthermore, the Examination Yuan should, within possible limits and based on the nature of each type of examination, select several key reference books for each subject to define the scope of questions for a certain number of years. This not only provides objective standards for examinations but also guides young people in their studies. In recent years, government-administered graduation exams for middle schools have yielded positive results. If this practice can be replicated for specialized schools and above, standards can be raised and unified, which will undoubtedly benefit the future of higher education. The state's recruitment exams may also consider these grades. However, this is a major undertaking that requires time for preparation. Therefore, it is proposed that starting in 1938, graduation exams for specialized schools and above be administered by the government, thereby establishing a connection with recruitment exams. Education in border provinces is less developed than in the interior. If admission is not made more lenient, there will be no widespread opportunity for talent to emerge, which may negatively impact political unity. A provincial breakdown of the personnel who passed the two higher-level exams held in the capital last year and the general exam held in the capital this year reveals the scarcity of recruits from border provinces. Therefore, the Examination Yuan should compile statistics on the number of educated people in each province every one or several years. For provinces where the ratio falls below a certain threshold, the standards should be lowered to allow for more lenient admission. This will allow talent from all over the country to advance equally, and the culture of border provinces can gradually improve. Specialized technical personnel are dedicated to their specific fields, and their performance in general subjects cannot be weighted equally with specialized subjects. Therefore, the examination procedures for such appointments should be modified. Specialized subjects should be tested first, allowing technical personnel to demonstrate their expertise and preventing the regret of overlooking talent due to slightly weaker performance in general subjects. The essence of constitutionalism lies in the exercise of civil rights, and the outcome of this exercise depends heavily on the knowledge and ability of candidates. As we approach the implementation of constitutionalism, we must diligently follow Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings and use examinations to assess the qualifications of candidates. However, there are many types of candidates, and election districts cover vast areas. General examination methods are difficult to apply. Therefore, candidate examinations should be divided into two types: screening and examination. In addition to written tests, methods such as qualification review and indirect examinations should be used as much as possible to ensure simplicity and feasibility. The specialized professions or technical personnel who are legally required to hold certificates have a significant impact on people's lives and property. These personnel were previously reviewed and registered by the competent authorities, who issued certificates. In the future, all such personnel should be examined or screened by the Examination Yuan. Those with competent authorities should first have their eligibility reviewed by the competent authorities. Those who pass the Examination Yuan examination will be issued a certificate of qualification and sent to the competent authority for legal registration. On the appointment side, the conference also made several important resolutions. Assessing administrative personnel according to definite and precise standards is an indispensable method for improving administrative efficiency. Furthermore, many civil servants in various agencies are currently recruited through recommendations rather than examinations, which inevitably leads to incompetence. Therefore, performance evaluations should be strictly enforced once a year, and a minimum elimination rate percentage should be set to clear the path to officialdom and promote the recruitment of qualified personnel who have passed the exams. Our country has a vast territory, and many localities rely on central government support. The implementation of all central government policies must be based on local conditions. However, there is a lack of connection between the central and local governments, and there is inevitable separation between the interior and the exterior. In recent years, intellectuals have flocked to the central government, making it difficult for remote provinces to recruit talent. Therefore, it has been decided to implement measures for the mutual transfer of civil servants between the central and local governments, so that the central government's intention to support local development and the principle of internal and external coordination are not merely empty words. The state must have definite standards for employing people. Therefore, there are regulations like the Civil Servant Appointment Law. However, due to the uneven levels of economic and cultural development in various regions and the insufficient distribution of personnel who have passed the exams and screenings, existing appointment regulations should be revised separately to broadly recruit talent and consider the facts. The means for expanding the qualifications for employment in remote provinces and regions, the manner for preferentially promoting Mongolian and Tibetan people, and the methods for broadly employing technical personnel and county assistants each have their specific circumstances and should be handled flexibly or through separate regulations. Appointing administrative personnel is a key function for employing people. Given the large number of officials in our country, it would be difficult to handle all appointment matters centrally. Entrusting them to the provinces would lack dedicated responsibility. To facilitate the promotion of appointments, appointment sub-offices should be established in each province, so that Dr. Sun Yat-sen's legacy that all civil servants in the central and local governments must have their qualifications determined before being appointed can be realized. Modern scholarship is constantly evolving. If civil servants cannot keep pace with the times, the implementation of agency policies may be out of sync with the times. Furthermore, talent levels vary depending on education. Cultivating scholarship in addition to official duties will greatly assist in the implementation of policies. Therefore, practical methods should be determined for how to universally promote and diligently implement continuing education for civil servants, so that it can be a goal for future efforts. Matters such as civil servant protection and pensions have also been carefully studied and appropriate plans have been agreed upon separately. The above are just some of the major points. Our conference does not seek lofty theories but rather practical and feasible solutions. All resolutions must be implemented. The central government uses this conference to understand the actual difficulties of the local governments, and the local governments use this conference to understand the spirit of the central government policies. From now on, internal and external matters will be consistent, so as to ensure the smooth implementation of the examination and appointment system. All those responsible for examination and appointment administration who participated in this conference are determined to implement the resolutions of this conference. We also hope that the people of the country will provide timely supervision. This declaration is hereby made. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 6th)

Current Commentary

Smuggling Chinese into the U.S. and American Exclusionary Immigration Laws

— Ting

Recently, thirty-eight overseas Chinese were smuggled into the United States from the British West Indian island of Trinidad. When the ship reached the American coast, four people became seriously ill and were thrown into the sea by the smugglers. Of the remaining thirty-four, eighteen have been discovered by U.S. government secret agents and will be deported back to China. The remaining sixteen have escaped the net and are also being hunted down.

This smuggling into the U.S. is known in the overseas Chinese community as "passing the barrier." The author spent two years in the West Indies and often heard news about overseas Chinese "passing the barrier." I have also spoken with overseas Chinese who have failed to "pass the barrier" many times. They are not unaware of the dangers of "passing the barrier," but despite the failures, people keep trying. The West Indies are located in the tropics. The only products are agricultural products such as sugar, tobacco, and coffee. In recent years, the supply of these products has exceeded demand, and prices have plummeted, which has affected the local economic prosperity. The livelihoods of overseas Chinese have been severely impacted, leading them to take desperate risks and "pass the barrier" to seek a living in the United States.

Before "passing the barrier," each overseas Chinese person must pay at least 500 U.S. dollars to the smugglers. They secretly board pre-arranged ships in remote locations under the cover of darkness. A small boat crowded with people tossed about on the tropical seas is already an inhumane existence. Moreover, they are afraid of being discovered by the outside world and can only crawl in the bottom of the hold, even struggling to survive in the coal piles. Sometimes, they set off from one location on an island and endure many days of hardship. Finally, someone on the boat says they have arrived in America. Then, they quietly disembark in the dark, thinking they have succeeded. Unexpectedly, when they open their eyes the next morning, they are still on the same island. The only thing that has changed is the location. They can only admit their bad luck. Sometimes, the ship enters U.S. territorial waters, and the customs patrol boat discovers them and comes to search. The smugglers, seeing that they cannot escape, tie up the "passengers" and throw them into the sea to feed the sharks. If the customs patrol boat is close by and throwing people into the sea might leave a trace, then they simply throw them into a raging furnace, instantly turning them into ashes.

Those who are lucky enough to reach the American coast "passing the barrier," but whose movements are not secret, are still discovered. At that time, they must still be imprisoned. After being tried and convicted, they are sent back to their original place. The government of their original country of residence often considers these "passing the barrier" overseas Chinese to be undesirable elements and does not allow them to re-enter the country, resulting in them ending up losing out on both ends. These poor creatures who are deported back to China are treated no differently from criminals on their way back to their country. And so-called returning to their country means only being sent to Shanghai. The overseas Chinese in the West Indies are almost entirely from Guangdong. The cost of traveling from Shanghai to Guangdong must be raised separately. The luckiest are those who safely cross the barrier. However, they can only live a clandestine life, unable to see the light of day. Especially during the "search and registration" period in "Chinatown," they feel even more embarrassed.

When we talk about the tragedy of Chinese people "passing the barrier," we cannot help but attribute it to the cruel American exclusionary immigration laws. Without these immigration laws, Chinese people could enter the United States as openly and honorably as Americans enter China. Why would they have to be so secretive?

There are three treaties between China and the United States regarding immigration. The first is the Burlingame Treaty of 1868. Article 5 of that treaty recognizes the right to change residence "as a natural and inalienable right." (According to the English translation.) It can be said to be the most equal treaty. The second is the Sino-American Supplementary Treaty of 1880. Article 1 of that treaty allows the United States to "regulate" or "limit" the number of Chinese laborers entering the United States and the number of years they can stay in the United States. However, it still clearly states that it "does not prohibit" Chinese laborers. Furthermore, that "limitation refers specifically to Chinese continuing to go to the United States to work as laborers. All other categories of people are not subject to restrictions." The third is the Chinese Labor Treaty of 1894. That treaty contains even more thorough provisions prohibiting Chinese laborers from entering the United States. However, that treaty was for a term of ten years. On January 24, 1904, the Chinese government declared that the treaty was null and void. Since 1904, there have been no new treaties between China and the United States regarding Chinese immigration. In other words, Chinese immigrants going to the United States should be treated in accordance with the Sino-American Supplementary Treaty of 1880 regarding laborers, and in accordance with the Burlingame Treaty of 1868 regarding non-laborers. However, the administrative and legislative authorities of the U.S. government have enacted and promulgated many extremely harsh domestic laws to restrict Chinese immigration, regardless of whether the content of the laws conflicts with the existing Sino-American treaties. According to the U.S. Constitution, treaties that the United States concludes with other countries and the laws of the federal government are considered the supreme law of the land. However, according to the precedent of the Washington Supreme Court, if domestic laws conflict with international treaties, the courts should judge cases based on the law or treaty that took effect last. If the treaty interests of a foreign government and people are thereby harmed, they can seek a solution through diplomatic means. The U.S. judicial authorities have no right to interfere. The U.S. government knows that China is not strong enough, and the Supreme Court is willing to indirectly and openly support it, so it dares to act as it pleases. However, treaties enjoy international legal protection, and the authority of a precedent of a national Supreme Court can never have the authority of international law. Moreover, the U.S. Supreme Court itself has clearly acknowledged that domestic laws that violate international treaties cannot have the effect of destroying the international treaty obligations that the United States has assumed. It can be seen that our country's tolerance of the American exclusionary immigration laws is entirely a matter of fact, not a matter of law. Even Americans cannot deny this.

The Sino-American Commercial Treaty of 1903 expired long ago. Negotiations for a new treaty have not made significant progress to this day. (See the author's article "The Key to Revising the Sino-American Commercial Treaty" in the "Current Commentary" section of this newspaper on February 2 of this year.) I remember that the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and the local Overseas Chinese Trust Company had petitioned the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to take the opportunity of the revision of the Sino-American treaty to negotiate the harsh American immigration rules. We also believe that our country has sufficient reason to negotiate with the U.S. government. Therefore, we dare to use the recent "passing the barrier" incident of overseas Chinese to once again draw the attention of the diplomatic authorities.

General Manager of Four Philippine Newspapers Arrives in Shanghai

[Nanjing] Mr. Froyle, the General Manager of four Philippine newspapers, took the night train to Shanghai on the 6th. It is said that Mr. Froyle will stay in Shanghai for about two weeks before returning to the Philippines. It is also said that after returning to the Philippines, Mr. Froyle will publish a special issue on China's recent situation. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 6th)

[Nanjing] Mr. Froyle, the General Manager of the Spanish-language Debate of the Philippines, the English-language Times, the American-language Weekly, and the Tagalog-language newspaper of the Philippines, came to China for a tour. He arrived in Shanghai a few days ago. On the morning of the 5th, he accompanied Mr. Li Dijun, Director of the Intelligence Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, from Shanghai to Beijing by train. Mr. Li led him to visit various places and met with the authorities on the evening of the 5th. Mr. Froyle met with Wang Shijie, Chen Shuren, and others on the 6th and was scheduled to return to Shanghai that evening. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 5th)

Three Ministries Plan to Restore the National Geodetic Survey Team

[Nanjing] After the establishment of the National Geodetic Survey Team, it was abolished due to financial difficulties. Recently, it was reported that the Ministries of Military Affairs, Interior, and Finance reconvened to discuss the matter and plan to re-establish it. The resolution has been submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 6th)

Liu Wendao Arrives in Shanghai from Beijing

[Nanjing] Liu Wendao and his wife took the night express train to Shanghai on the evening of the 6th. They will stay in Shanghai for two or three days and then travel to Hangzhou for sightseeing. After that, they will return to their hometown of Wuxue for a trip. The departure date for their trip abroad is set for December 20th. Tickets have been pre-booked with the China Travel Service. (Special dispatch on the 6th)

Bank Savings Committee Appoints Real Estate Expert

[Nanjing] In order to ensure the security of savings deposits, the Bank Savings Deposit Guarantee Reserve Fund Committee must conduct a thorough investigation of the real estate used as collateral by various savings institutions. The committee has now appointed Kui Yanfang as a special commissioner to review real estate matters and has sent a letter to the Ministry of Finance for filing. (Special dispatch on the 6th)

China Reclamation Bank's Beijing Branch Launches Small Agricultural, Industrial, and Commercial Loans

[Nanjing] The China Reclamation Bank is launching small agricultural, industrial, and commercial loans in Beijing. Each loan is for 100 yuan, and each person cannot borrow more than two loans. The monthly interest rate is 0.9%, the term is six months, and the handling fee is 1%. The guarantor is limited to shopkeepers. (Special dispatch on the 6th)

Ministry of Finance Plans to Draft Tax Anti-Smuggling Regulations

[Nanjing] Recently, the Ministry of Finance believes that smuggling is becoming increasingly prevalent, which has a significant impact on customs revenue. It has expedited the drafting of the Provisional Regulations on Tax Anti-Smuggling and the Provisional Regulations on Punishing Smuggling and submitted them to the Executive Yuan for approval and then to the Central Political Conference for approval. (Special dispatch on the 6th)

Lianyungang Project to Be Completed Soon

[Nanjing] According to transportation circles, the Lianyungang project is nearing completion. The foundation of the pier is extremely solid. Since the start of berthing on October 1, cargo transportation has been booming. The total volume of imports and exports has reached over 10,000 tons per month, all of which are local products from Jiangsu, Shandong, Henan, and Shaanxi provinces. Currently, only one 3,000-ton seagoing vessel can be docked. The remaining parts of the project are still in progress. The completion of the pier by the end of this year will allow for the docking of three vessels. The entire harbor project can be completed by next spring, allowing for the docking of eight vessels. Currently, the Longhai Railway and the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company are jointly operating land-sea transportation to promote the development of shipping and provide for the import and export of goods from the northwest and southwest. The plan is to complete and open three shipping routes: one from Lianyungang directly to Tianjin, one from Lianyungang directly to Qingdao, and one from Lianyungang directly to Guangzhou, passing through Shanghai. This has been approved by the Ministry of Communications and the Ministry of Railways. (Special dispatch on the 6th)

Ministry of Railways' Business Department Completes Study on Freight Reclassification

[Nanjing] The Business Department of the Ministry of Railways has completed its study on freight reclassification, including freight rates and the packaging of light goods. It is also planning to reduce the classification of imported machinery and appropriately increase or decrease the classification of luxury goods. The remaining methods are being studied, and a list of light and heavy goods will be drafted within a week and submitted to various railways for practical study to determine their classification. (Special dispatch on the 6th)

Women's Legal Movement in the Capital

[Nanjing] The Capital Women's League for Legal Equality held a committee meeting on the 6th and passed a declaration and sent a telegram to women's circles across the country, unanimously rising up and vowing to fight to the death against the amendment to the Criminal Law on adultery. The Boxer Protocol Does Not Explicitly Stipulate That British Troops Abandon Exercises Outside the Great Wall

Simeon's Statement in the House of Commons

[London] During today's House of Commons meeting, Labour MP Jones inquired about the fact that the commander of the British troops in Shanhaiguan received a note from local Japanese representatives and the Manchu authorities on June 26 of this year, stating that British troops should not enter "Manchukuo." How is the British government handling this matter? Foreign Secretary Simeon replied that the British government has decided that British troops should abandon the practice of conducting exercises outside the Great Wall. The Boxer Protocol of September 7, 1901, does not explicitly permit this. The British government does not want to raise legal issues for discussion, so it has made this decision. Suitable exercise grounds can be found inside the Great Wall (the crowd laughed). Simeon ended by saying that he had no reason to believe that the government's decision would change. This "prohibition" also applies to the troops of other countries. (Reuters dispatch on the 4th)

Case of Forbidding British Newspaper

Liberal MP Raises Questions

[London] The Harbin Daily, run by Simpson, was recently banned from publication by the "Manchu" authorities. During today's House of Commons meeting, Liberal MP Mond raised questions about this matter. Foreign Secretary Simeon replied that the government has instructed the British Consul-General in Harbin, Garstin, to consult with Simpson and then make a request to the "Manchu" authorities. The "Manchu" authorities recently accused the newspaper of communist propaganda and banned its publication and attempted to expel its reporter and publisher, Simpson. Simpson fled to the British Consulate-General and then voluntarily went to Dalian. (Reuters dispatch on the 5th)

British and American Oil Companies Act in Concert with Japan

Before the Monopoly Law Is Promulgated

Intended to Negotiate a Compromise

[London] Oil companies are hopeful regarding Japan's reply to British and American protests about the "Manchukuo" kerosene monopoly. It is said that the monopoly law has not yet been formally promulgated, and there is a possibility of negotiating a compromise that preserves the face of "Manchukuo" while protecting the interests of foreign oil companies and allowing the Manchurian Oil Company and the Dalian Refinery to obtain an appropriate share of the business. In this situation, oil companies are convinced that Japan's insistence that the proposed monopoly is an internal policy of "Manchukuo" and does not refer to the Nine-Power Treaty is intentional to avoid complex diplomatic disputes and serious repercussions for the naval conference. Oil companies believe that the path has been opened for British and American consuls stationed in Manchuria to negotiate a compromise in Changchun. As for rumors that the Japanese are now trying to alienate Britain and the United States, oil companies dismiss them with a smile, saying that foreign oil companies are now acting in concert. (Reuters dispatch on the 6th)

British Side Considers Japan's Reply Unsatisfactory

[London] It is reported that the Japanese government has replied to the British government's protest against the new law on the Japanese government's control of domestic kerosene companies. The British side considers the reply unsatisfactory. Although there is no basis for opposition in the treaty, the governments of Britain, the United States, and the Netherlands all believe that it is unfair for the Japanese government to treat the important kerosene industry in this way. (Reuters dispatch on the 5th)

Japan's Military Build-up Treats Mandated Territories as Forbidden Areas

Report of the League of Nations Committee of Inquiry

Chairman Asks for Opening Up to Dispel Doubts

[Geneva] After the League of Nations' Committee on Mandates met this morning to discuss the Japanese government's report on the Pacific islands formerly owned by Germany under mandate, it held a closed meeting for two hours. During that time, the issue of Japan's appropriation of 800,000 yuan to build docks and airfields was raised. The chairman, the Italian representative, Ciotri, asked whether foreign aircraft could land on these islands. The Japanese representative, Ito, did not give a definite answer to this question. The chairman also said that Japan currently prohibits foreigners from traveling to these islands, or allows them to travel but subjects them to strict surveillance. This kind of news has been reported with great certainty. If you want to end it, the best way is to cancel all bans. Ito replied that many of the reports about this matter were intentional. The Japanese authorities had to implement special plans because the islands were not peaceful, which may have been the case. Ito also said that the Japanese Navy had conducted exercises near these islands at some time, so it did not want foreigners to travel there. As for the case of a certain British clergyman being prohibited from traveling to the islands within his religious jurisdiction, he would investigate it. (Central-Transocean News Agency dispatch on the 5th)

[Geneva] Japan has submitted an annual report to the League of Nations on the situation of its mandate over the Pacific Islands. The Committee on Mandates of the League of Nations has reviewed it. The Japanese representative, Minister to Warsaw Ito, attended to explain. Recently, newspapers have reported that Japan has been making things difficult for foreigners and ships traveling to the ports of the various islands in the Pacific under Japanese rule. Mr. Ito explained this matter, saying that these reports have other motives and should not be lightly believed. As for other special circumstances, he will explain them in detail after he has investigated them thoroughly. The chairman of the committee said that the world's newspapers have been criticizing the internal situation of the islands under Japanese mandate in the Pacific. For Japan's sake, it would be advisable to find a way to dispel the doubts of the world. The best way to quell the rumors is to open up the islands and allow foreigners to enter and exit freely. The committee requested Japan to supplement its explanation because the annual report submitted by Japan was incomplete in content. (Note: The criticism of the world's newspapers probably refers to the military installations set up by Japan in the islands under its mandate in the Pacific.) (Havas dispatch on the 5th)

United States Pays Close Attention

Unwilling to Express an Opinion for the Time Being

[Washington] When the League of Nations Committee on Mandates was meeting, someone asked the State Department about the U.S. attitude toward the former German territories in the Pacific under Japanese mandate. The State Department official spoke evasively, unwilling to give a direct answer, only saying that this issue was "very specialized" and required the interpretation of the League of Nations, so the United States was unwilling to express an opinion. As for the rumors spread in Geneva that Japan had closed off two mandated islands in the South Pacific and prohibited foreigners from entering the port, the Undersecretary of State was also unwilling to confirm or deny them. (National Telegram on the 5th)

Japan Issues Statement

Prohibiting Foreign Ships from Sailing

Said Not to Violate Mandate Regulations

[Tokyo] On the 5th, the League of Nations Committee on Mandates accused Japan of illegal acts in its mandated islands in the South Seas. The spokesman of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs issued the following statement today: The Japanese government abides by the mandate regulations and has not violated the law. The accusations of the League of Nations Committee on Mandates are unfounded. Foreigners are free to land on the islands under Japanese mandate and have not been prohibited from doing so. Also, regarding the navigation of foreign ships, because the islands are designated routes for the government, only Japanese ships are allowed to sail. There should be no problem with this either. (China United Press dispatch on the 6th)

Naval Negotiations Deadlocked, Britain Efforts to Mediate

Simon Meets Separately with U.S. and Japanese Representatives

Japanese Government Actively Preparing Treaty Abolition Procedures

[London] British Foreign Secretary Simon and U.S. Representative Davis discussed the deadlock in the British, American, and Japanese naval talks in the House of Commons this afternoon. This discussion has garnered considerable attention, as it is widely hoped that Simon can devise a plan to keep the naval talks going. (Reuters, 6th)

[London] Through the efforts of British diplomats, the naval talks may resume today. Foreign Secretary Simon will invite Japanese Ambassador Matsudaira to a private meeting to propose a plan to continue the talks. The U.S. delegation also learned of this news from Simon's side today. Britain is likely to open a path for Japan, allowing Japan to propose a suggestion similar to what its ambassador, Saitō, recently did in Washington: that Japan actually desires to achieve naval equality over a number of years. If so, the U.S. representatives would be happy to participate in the talks. However, the U.S. representatives now state that they will do nothing but listen. The general public now feels that the talks will not fail or remain deadlocked for long and will eventually reach a compromise. However, this compromise may be insignificant.

When a spokesman for the U.S. delegation met with a Reuters correspondent today, the correspondent asked whether there was any possibility of a compromise between the U.S. and Japan regarding naval ratios and whether there was any hope for a satisfactory outcome of the talks. The spokesman replied, "Sometimes there is no compromise, and sometimes there is a compromise." His words were ambiguous and elusive. It is widely expected that Britain will step into the gap to find a way to achieve an outcome. Although Britain's views are closer to Japan's, Britain is now eager for the three countries to maintain the talks and avoid a breakdown. Japan has no room for maneuver because it insists on its demand for equality, as it feels it cannot change its position or back down for the sake of national dignity.

Japanese Representative Matsudaira's attitude is more moderate, and he is quite willing to make a slightly broader request for equality. However, the extremely nationalistic army and navy officers in his country view him as too moderate and will not allow him to place too much emphasis on diplomatic friendship. Since Matsudaira's actions are not free, he hopes that Britain will find a way to mediate and formulate a plan that contains Japan's more moderate demands and is also acceptable to the UK and the US. At the same time, Matsudaira also warned his government not to hastily announce the abolition of the Washington Naval Treaty. While the abolition will eventually take place within the year, it will not be announced in London for the time being. Before this bombshell drops, all parties will still try their best to keep the London talks going. The Washington Naval Treaty stipulates that a conference of all naval powers must be convened within one year of the abolition. At that time, the Washington and London naval treaties will expire. The conference venue will be either in London or Washington, with London being more suitable. The time will be in the summer of next year. (Reuters, 6th)

[Tokyo] The issue of abolishing the Washington Treaty was passed by the Naval Military Council on the 29th and by the Marshal Council on the 31st. Now, only the approval procedure of the Privy Council remains, and it is confirmed that the abolition will be announced at the end of this month or the beginning of next month. (Japan United Press, 6th)

Dutch Representative Condemns Japan's Monopoly in the Far East

Strongly Advocates Boycotting Japanese Goods

The Hague: Dutch Ministry of Economic Affairs representative史左傑 (Shi Zuojie, phonetic transliteration) recently returned from Batavia and strongly criticized Japan's expansion of political and economic influence in the Pacific, especially in the Dutch territories. Mr.史氏 represents the Netherlands in trade negotiations with Japan. Mr.史氏 claimed that the Dutch East Indies has prepared import quotas for 54 types of Japanese goods and said that "we must squeeze out the Japanese, whether the Japanese are willing or not, they must accept our quotas." "One hundred percent of the Japanese in the Dutch East Indies are consolidating their sphere of influence. Japan's goal is to control the East Indies' commerce. The Japanese cannot separate commerce from politics, so they regard themselves as the rulers of the East. This concept can be seen in their behavior in the East Indies. The success or failure of Japanese-Dutch commercial negotiations will depend on how much of the East Indies' products Japan is willing to purchase. All the warehouses in Batavia are full of Japanese goods. I personally doubt whether the Dutch and Japanese can compromise." However, I do not deny that cheap Japanese goods have their place in the East Indies. (National News Agency, 5th)

Batavia: Japanese Representative 越田 (Yueshita, phonetic transliteration) met with Dutch East Indies Representative 海德連 (Haidelian, phonetic transliteration) at 6 p.m. on the 5th to discuss the report issue, but the two sides could not reach an agreement. The Japanese delegation, in an effort to overcome the difficulties, requested instructions from its home government and, at the same time, secretly prepared to return home in anticipation of the worst-case scenario. (United Press, 5th)

Britain Urges China to Pay Overdue Railway Loans

[London] Foreign Secretary Simon replied to a question from Conservative MP Mullen in the House of Commons today, saying that the 790,000 pounds of the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway loan that expired on July 1st, and the 2,182,000 pounds of the British portion of the Tianjin-Pukou Railway loan that also expired, have not been paid. British Ambassador to China Cadogan has repeatedly inquired with the Chinese government, and will continue to urge payment in the future. (Reuters, 5th)

Core Group of Disarmament Conference to Convene on the 20th of This Month

Discussing Revision of Working Procedures

Points Where Compromise is Currently Hoped For

Separate Protocols Will Be Established First

[Geneva] The League of Nations Secretariat issued a statement this afternoon signed by Henderson, Chairman of the Disarmament Conference, stating that the discussion of the disarmament issue should be extended to after the beginning of next year. The statement calls for the Disarmament Presidium to meet during the special session of the League of Nations Assembly (scheduled to open on November 20). The Secretariat suggests incorporating certain issues that are expected to be agreed upon separately into protocols, which can be implemented separately without waiting for the Disarmament Conference to complete a convention. Examples include regulations on the arms trade, publication issues, and the establishment of a permanent disarmament committee. The statement concludes by saying that work on the aviation issue should begin as soon as possible. (Reuters, 5th)

[Geneva] Henderson, Chairman of the Disarmament Conference, has sent a document to the representatives of the Presidium countries to revise the working procedures of the Disarmament Conference. The League of Nations Secretariat has now published this document, which states that when the Disarmament Conference passed the compromise proposal of the United Kingdom, France, and the United States in early June of this year, it was decided to continue negotiations in order to establish a general disarmament convention. These negotiations were originally undertaken enthusiastically by former French Foreign Minister Barthou in a faithful manner. However, the assassination in Marseille occurred, and Barthou was tragically killed, causing these negotiations to be delayed. Given the situation, it is specifically suggested that the disarmament issue and the negotiations for establishing a general disarmament convention be postponed until the spring of 1935 before they are concluded. As for the points that have already been thoroughly considered, it is permissible to establish protocols in advance. The so-called points that have already been thoroughly considered are (1) the control and manufacturing of weapons; (2) the disclosure of military budgets; (3) the organization of a standing disarmament committee. In addition, the disarmament conference resolution in June of this year advocated the banning of state-owned aviation, but research has not yet begun on this level. This level is particularly important and should be reviewed as soon as possible. The Presidium is scheduled to meet on November 20. At that time, all members should express their opinions. (Havas, 5th)

British House of Commons Discusses Saar Situation

Germany and France Take Cautious Measures

British Government Expresses Satisfaction

[London] When the British House of Commons discussed the tense situation in the Saar today, Foreign Secretary Simon replied to a question from opposition leader Lansbury, saying that the Saar Governing Commission is responsible for the security of the Saar. The Saar plebiscite is scheduled to be held on January 13 next year. This responsibility for maintaining order will still be borne by the Commission. The situation where the Saar Commission feels unable to maintain order should not occur. He believes that it will certainly not happen. The Saar Commission stated to the League of Nations Council as early as 1926 that the Commission had the right to convene troops on the border and nearby to assist in maintaining order when absolutely necessary. The League of Nations Council recorded this document. Any military action by France outside the Saar is purely precautionary. If the Governing Commission cannot fulfill its responsibilities and is forced to ask for assistance, then the use of foreign troops to maintain order is not a problem. As for borrowing British troops, it was not even mentioned.

The British Foreign Secretary also informed the House of Commons that the German Ambassador has confirmed today the reports that the German government has prohibited the Nazi stormtroopers and the Black Guard from wearing uniforms within 25 miles of the Saar border during the plebiscite. At the same time, the French Ambassador also stated firmly that there was no danger of invading the Saar region. Simon concluded, "I have expressed to the German and French ambassadors the British government's satisfaction with these statements. At the same time, I received a letter from the French Ambassador, stating firmly that France's preparations are purely precautionary. Under these circumstances, we can believe that the Saar plebiscite will be conducted in a stable situation with careful handling from all sides." (Reuters, 5th)

Democratic Party Likely to Win U.S. Elections

U.S. Election Tragedy

Republicans Sniped at Democrats

Resulting in Four Deaths and Twenty-Two Injuries

Kieres, Pennsylvania: An election tragedy occurred in this small town today. Democrats held a campaign parade and were machine-gunned by the opposing party, killing four and injuring twenty-two. This massacre was the culmination of a conflict between local Democratic and Republican leaders. Five hundred marchers were demonstrating on the main street when, at a corner in front of Republican leader Bai Lunna's (phonetic transliteration) house, machine-gun fire suddenly erupted. Many marchers were hit and fell to the ground. Two people died on the spot, and two others died on the way to the hospital. Twenty-two people were injured, three of whom are not expected to survive. Local authorities could not cope and urgently requested assistance from the state troops. However, before the state troops arrived, the enraged miners attacked Bai Lunna's house but could not break in. Just as they were about to blow up the house, the state troops arrived, dispersed the crowd, stormed the house, and arrested 14 members of the Bai Lunna family, confiscating many weapons such as machine guns, rifles, and pistols. The town is now under de facto martial law, with state troops and local police patrolling the streets to prevent the crowd from carrying out lynchings. (National News Agency, 5th)

Sino-U.S. Trade Decreases

[Washington] According to statistics released today, trade between China and the United States in September decreased compared to the same month last year. U.S. exports to China this month were US$3,970,000, and imports were US$3,470,000. Exports in the same month last year were US$4,671,000, and imports were US$3,800,000. Total U.S. exports in September were US$191,000,000, and total imports were US$131,000,000. Exports in the same month last year were US$160,000,000, and imports were US$146,000,000. Exports to the UK totaled US$40,000,000, an increase of US$12,000,000 compared to the same month last year. Imports from the U.S. decreased from US$12,000,000 last year to US$9,000,000. Exports to Japan have increased from US$15,000,000 last year to US$20,000,000. Imports from Japan in September were US$12,000,000, a decrease of US$2,000,000 compared to the same month last year. (Reuters, 5th)

Regarding the issue of the period for supplying goods, the Soviet Union is now willing to concede to three years from the original two and a half years. Regarding the issue of consulates and other cultural facilities affiliated with the Chinese Eastern Railway, the Soviet Union expressed some concessions. As for issues such as the property catalog and loan comparison table, the cause is that this party provided a reply. However, because the fundamental issue of payment guarantees was not agreed upon, the Japanese side did not provide a reply. Moreover, Foreign Minister Hirota was busy attending cabinet meetings, so the meeting was temporarily suspended and the two parted at 2:20 p.m. They will continue discussions at the next opportunity. Fate of French Cabinet Hangs in the Balance

Refuses to Compromise with Premier Doumergue

[Paris] It is widely expected that Herriot and other Radical Party cabinet members will resign this afternoon. (Reuters, 6th)

[Paris] The Doumergue cabinet is currently facing the possibility of a cabinet crisis. According to reliable sources, during the State Council meeting this morning, Minister without Portfolio Herriot stated that his political friends did not agree with Premier Doumergue's suggestion that voting in favor of the provisional budget bill should be regarded as supporting the constitutional reform bill. At that time, Premier Doumergue asked Herriot whether the Radical Socialist Party cabinet members would resign. After the Radical Socialist Party cabinet members left the meeting to discuss, they agreed to postpone the decision on whether to resign until the State Council meeting on Thursday morning. Therefore, the government will make a final decision on Thursday. Before that, the Radical Socialist Party parliamentary group will meet to discuss. If Herriot continues to reject Premier Doumergue's proposed procedure, the entire cabinet may resign. (Havas, 6th)

[Paris] According to reliable political sources, the political fate of Premier Doumergue will be decided at today's administrative meeting. Today's administrative meeting is chaired by President Lebrun. If the Radical Socialist Party cabinet members cannot compromise on Doumergue's policies, Doumergue will inevitably resign. Doumergue is also aware of this, so he has already drafted his resignation letter in preparation. The Radical Party in the Chamber of Deputies will meet this afternoon to discuss how to respond to Doumergue's constitutional reform bill. It is reported that there are only three options: (1) vote against Doumergue's reform bill; (2) abstain from voting; (3) allow each individual to act freely. If the last option is adopted, Doumergue's cabinet policy may gain the support of the majority. (National News Agency, 6th)

Parliament Opened Yesterday

Expressed Condolences for the Death of the King of South

Budget Bill Postponed Until Tomorrow for Discussion

[Paris] The State Council met this morning, chaired by President Lebrun. Premier Doumergue presented the draft of the speech to be read in the Chamber of Deputies in the afternoon. When the Chamber of Deputies met in the afternoon, the Speaker will present eulogies for the former King Alexander of Yugoslavia, the late Foreign Minister Barthou, and the former President Poincaré. Then, Premier Doumergue will read the speech, which will briefly state that no pain experienced by Europe has exceeded the tragic loss of the King of South. Alexander was a benevolent ruler of Yugoslavia, a true founding father, and a craftsman of peace. As for Yugoslavia, the people's calmness and solemnity can be regarded as a model. No matter who, they should provide assistance to the Southern Kingdom so that it can see the light. The conclusion is that although the King of South is dead, his policies are not dead. When Alexander passed away, he still cried out, "Save Yugoslavia quickly!" The people of France and the Southern Kingdom should always remember this sentence. (Havas, 6th)

[Paris] The French government's plan has changed again. Premier Doumergue's budget bill, originally scheduled for discussion on Wednesday, has now been postponed to 8 p.m. on Thursday. The reason is that a committee will be convened first on Wednesday. According to sources in Parliament, this delay is Doumergue's strategy to appease opposition to the constitutional reform bill, especially the Radical Socialist Party. Tomorrow, Doumergue will submit the initial draft of this reform to the Speaker of the Chamber of Deputies so that it can be discussed on that day. It is also reported that Doumergue will deliver a speech in the Chamber of Deputies on Thursday and ask the Chamber to hold a vote of confidence. (National News Agency, 5th)

Internal Opinions of the Radical Socialist Party Differ

[Paris] The French cabinet met this morning, and the Radical Socialist Party also held a meeting in the afternoon. There are new developments in the political situation. Premier Doumergue is determined not to easily abandon his position, acting as a pillar in the whirlpool of conspiracies and rumors. It is reported that Finance Minister 馬旦 (Madan, phonetic transliteration) does not agree with the Premier's approach of not dealing with the budget first and instead asking for funds, and he is unwilling to present this bill in the Chamber of Deputies. The Radical Socialist Party is divided into two factions: some are dissatisfied with the actions similar to a dictatorship, while others do not want to be responsible for the political turmoil that would occur if Doumergue resigned. Therefore, their steps may not be consistent. It is expected that there will be a major battle when the Radical Socialist Party meets this afternoon. Rumors are rife, and the stock market is sluggish. The people are suffering from political conspiracies and commercial instability, and they are becoming increasingly unbearable. (Reuters, 6th)

However, regarding the extension of the validity of the budget bill by the government (Premier Doumergue argued that if the budget bill is not passed by both houses before January 1 of the relevant year, the government may extend all or part of the previous year's budget by order of law), it made a reservation, saying that "the power to approve the expenditure of public funds belongs to the representatives of the people." In addition, the United Federation believes that it is inappropriate for the Premier to include the civil servant protection clause in the Constitution. The conclusion of its declaration is that "the United Federation does not want to see France fall into extremes, but does not know the way to compromise. The so-called extremes are long-standing habits or the establishment of personal power." (Havas, 6th)

One-Week Session Starting on the 27th of This Month

Plan to Reduce Public Debt Will Be in Vain

[Tokyo] As a result of consultations between Prime Minister Okada and Chief Cabinet Secretary Yoshida on the evening of the 5th, it was decided to convene a special Diet on November 27 for a seven-day session. After the cabinet officially decides on the 6th, it will be submitted to the Emperor for approval.

Since the Kansai wind disaster and other disaster relief budget proposals have been submitted by various provinces to the Ministry of Finance, Finance Minister Fujii plans to review them together with the basic budget. This disaster budget is calculated in the form of supplementary budgets for several years, such as fiscal year 9, fiscal year 10, or fiscal year 11, so it is difficult to separate the fiscal year 9 budget and submit it to the special Diet for review. The approximate amount of this budget is 120 million yuan for fiscal year 9, 150 million yuan for fiscal year 10, and 30 million yuan each year thereafter, totaling about 300 million yuan. Finance Minister Fujii has stated that he acknowledges 100 million yuan in the disaster budget and has decided on a policy to reduce public debt. It seems difficult to satisfy the relief for rural areas across the country.

The amount of public debt that the Ministry of Finance plans to issue in the next fiscal year is 604 million yuan, a decrease of 206 million yuan compared to the fixed amount of 810 million yuan in this fiscal year. However, various provinces will need to revive their original budget proposals, and disaster relief budgets also need to issue public debt, so the future does not allow optimism. Finance Minister Fujii plans to acknowledge 100 million yuan for the revival request, disaster budget, and delivery of public debt, so the deficit public debt issued for the revival request seems to reach more than 50 million yuan. The amount of public debt in fiscal year 10 is also close to 810 million yuan. According to the authorities' investigation, the existing amount of national debt at the end of September this year was 8,335,602,000 yuan, plus the planned issuance amount of 600 million yuan this year, 604 million yuan in fiscal year 10, and disaster and other budgets, which will reach almost 10 billion yuan. The government's plan to reduce the issuance of public debt will be in vain. (Japan United Press, 6th)
