Hunan Fellow Association Submits a Letter of Petition for Relief

The Hunan Fellow Association in Shanghai submitted multiple letters and telegrams to the central government, the National Government Relief Committee, and various ministries and commissions yesterday, seeking relief for the drought in Hunan Province. More than a thousand letters were sent to charitable organizations in various places, Hunan Fellow Associations in various places, charitable organizations in Shanghai, public legal entities, newspapers, and fellows. The letter stated: "It has only been two years since the Xinwei flood, and the local vitality has yet to recover, and the people's breathing has not yet settled. However, there is also an unprecedented drought in more than 60 counties this year. Not only are remote mountain villages in despair of the autumn harvest, but even the counties that are known to be relatively fertile have no grain harvest. The old and weak are in the ravines, and epidemics are spreading, with cries reaching hundreds of miles away, as cruel as entering the eighteenth hell. Refugees are scattered, with tears falling down. It is our unavoidable duty to open the granaries and request grain. Our association respectfully appeals to all charitable people and gentlemen in our country. We beg you to have mercy on these remnants and provide prompt relief. Even a grain or a thread is enough to save a person's life. It is more than just repaying the kindness by tying grass or carrying a ring in our mouths. If all the kind people from all walks of life donate money and goods for relief, please send them directly to the Hunan Drought Relief Committee in Changsha for inspection and receipt, in order to be simple, straightforward, and prudent. Our association respectfully thanks all the disaster-stricken people in Hunan on their knees. We express our words with tears, hoping for universal relief. We respectfully wish you good fortune. We cannot express our gratitude. The Hunan Fellow Association in Shanghai respectfully bows, Standing Committee Members Zhou Zhenlin, Ye Kaixin, Chen Jie, Huang Yi'ou, Shen Zunuo, Chen Heting, and Li Zhi."

Famine Victims in Haining Eat Barnyard Grass to Survive

Some Use the Seeds of the Stink Tree as Food

Most Self-Sufficient Farmers Are Not Eligible for Relief

This year's disaster in Haining is extraordinarily severe, and the tragic situation has only recently become fully apparent. Although the Shanghai Haining Drought Relief Association has been working hard to raise funds and has requested assistance from the Jisheng Society, the Sino-Foreign Relief Association, the Bodhi Benevolent Society, and the Red Swastika Society to jointly carry out emergency relief efforts, reports from those who have returned to Shanghai from the disaster area indicate that the majority of villagers have reached a point where they have nothing to eat. They are gathering barnyard grass seeds from the fields, which are commonly found in rice paddies and are usually sifted out and discarded, but in times of famine, they are considered a superior food source. In the Yuanhua Town area of the Third District, bordering Haiyan, people are even gathering the seeds of the stink tree (Ailanthus altissima), which resemble chestnuts and are thus known as "wild chestnuts." In the past, these were used as firewood or to feed pigs, but even the pigs did not like to eat them. Now, they are being used as food for people. What is even more ridiculous is that when the Third District Public Office was reviewing the list of disaster victims, they ordered all the village police officers to gather at the office and ask each household if they had any grain. Those who owned three or four mu of land were not eligible for relief. As a result, the average self-sufficient farmer, who has no harvest this year and is suffering as much as the tenant farmers, is being treated very differently from the tenant farmers when it comes to receiving relief. It is said that the district originally reported over 110,000 disaster-stricken households, but after a closed-door review, regardless of the severity of the disaster, the list was drastically reduced, leaving only twenty-odd thousand. As a result, a large number of disaster victims are still without relief. Next year's rice seeds are already gone due to this year's lack of harvest, and even those who have a small amount left are struggling to survive in the present and have nothing to spare. Therefore, seeds have also become a problem. The time to the next harvest is at least half a year away, and only public works projects can alleviate the urgent needs of the disaster victims. It is said that the association has realized that this year's drought was caused by the high terrain and riverbeds, which prevented water from the west (such as the Tiaoxi River) and the east (such as the Mao River) from flowing in. The severe drought lasted for four months, almost cutting off the drinking water supply. Now that relief is not a short-term matter, it is fortunate that the Zhejiang Provincial Government has allocated 11.1 million yuan in public bonds specifically for public works projects in the disaster area. The association has submitted a detailed report to the provincial government, requesting the allocation of funds to carry out public works projects to improve water conservancy and save the disaster victims.

Recent News on Jisheng Society's Relief Efforts in Haining

The Chinese Jisheng Society, recognizing the severity of the drought in Haining, is jointly carrying out emergency relief efforts with the Sino-Foreign Relief Association and the Haining Drought Relief Association. Yesterday, they received a report from Director Li Yunmen in Shanghai, stating that the disaster situation in the county is extremely serious. A preliminary investigation of the Fifth District found 17,800 households, each with anywhere from five or six to seven or eight members, totaling a large number of people. The limited relief funds available are insufficient to meet the needs, and more funds are urgently needed. The report also mentioned a lack of relief workers and requested additional personnel. In response, the Jisheng Society has added three relief workers, Fan Shoumin, Yin Shunzhang, and Shi Kelong, who departed today. Regarding the request for additional relief funds, the Society is facing a shortage of funds and is unable to provide immediate assistance. They are currently making urgent appeals, hoping that benevolent individuals and organizations will come to their rescue. Saving even one life is an act of great merit, and the true rewards are immeasurable.

Magistrate Luo Zhongda of Chongde County Comes to Shanghai to Beg for Relief

Luo Zhongda, the magistrate of Chongde County in Zhejiang Province, came to Shanghai yesterday to beg for relief from all sectors of society, as the disaster situation in his area is extraordinarily severe. A reporter from the New Voice Newspaper met with Magistrate Luo at his lodging yesterday. Luo said that the county has a total of 290,000 mu of paddy fields, of which 210,000 mu have been affected by the disaster, with 73,000 mu having no harvest at all. The Fourth and Fifth Districts are the worst affected, with 40,000 and 89 extremely poor people on the verge of starvation if not rescued, and another 26,000 somewhat poor people. Disaster victims from the Fourth District are carrying baskets and walking sticks, begging for food along the roads. Robberies are rampant, and grave robbing and coffin looting are common sights. If relief is not provided urgently, they will all freeze and starve to death. He has come to Shanghai to beg for relief from the Sino-Foreign Relief Association, the Zhejiang Drought Relief Association, and the Red Swastika Society to help the tens of thousands of disaster victims in his county who are suffering in dire straits.

Fellow Villagers of Luhe County in Shanghai Establish a Drought Relief Committee

Luhe County in Jiangsu Province has suffered an extraordinarily severe drought this year, leaving farmers with no harvest. Fellow villagers of Luhe County in Shanghai, including Dong Xiujia, Xia Yizhai, Huang Zhong, Chen Lingyi, and Li Huating, have established a Drought Relief Committee for the county. The following is the original text of their announcement appealing for donations: "Respectfully announcing, Luhe suffered a drought in 1929, followed by a flood in 1931. In 1932 and 1933, droughts and floods occurred frequently, reducing harvests. Combined with low grain prices, the people's suffering has not been alleviated, leaving nine out of ten households empty and the rural economy bankrupt. This year, since the beginning of summer, there has been no rain at all. Rivers have dried up, and ditches and ponds are empty. Beans sprouted and withered immediately, and rice seedlings withered before planting. No grass is green, and the entire land is desolate. Luhe is a remote and barren area in northern Jiangsu, and it cannot withstand repeated disasters. After the autumn harvest, there were occasional showers, and farmers managed to borrow money to buy mung beans and buckwheat, planting them as much as possible, hoping to salvage some of the harvest. However, before the seedlings emerged, they were damaged by insects. Those that were not damaged by insects were subjected to more than ten days of continuous rain, causing the roots to rot. There is no hope for a new harvest, and there are no old reserves. Luhe is divided into seven districts. Except for a small area of polder fields along the river in the southeast corner of the Third District, which had a slight harvest, the remaining six districts, bordering Tianchang and Lai'an in Anhui Province, and Jiangpu in this province, have become a desolate wasteland with no harvest. Residents, seeing that there is no hope for survival, have left their homes and scattered in all directions. Those who have no way to make a living and no way to find food have become starving refugees on the roads, a sight too tragic to bear. Some have gone without food for days, unable to get a full meal, and have closed their doors and committed suicide. It is heartbreaking to hear. We, who live in Shanghai, have repeatedly received letters and telegrams from our hometown begging for relief, and we feel the pain deeply. Although we have tried our best to raise funds, our capabilities are limited, and it is a drop in the bucket, insufficient to solve the problem. Furthermore, the future is long, and winter is approaching. If we do not quickly seek relief, the dying refugees will face starvation and freezing, and all will perish. We humbly implore all benevolent individuals and philanthropists to have compassion and fulfill their generous wishes, donating grain and contributing money to save our disaster victims, so that they may escape death and be reborn, and all will be grateful for your kindness. As the saying goes, 'Saving one life is better than building a ten-level pagoda.' Your great kindness will bring immeasurable merit. We, the members of the committee, bow our heads nine times to beg for the people of Luhe."

Chinese Cigarette Industry Requests Cancellation of Cigarette Surtax in Shaanxi Province

Shaanxi Province Heavily Imposes a 40% Surtax

Telegraphic Request to the Tax Bureau to Forward a Letter of Cancellation

The Shanghai Chinese Cigarette Industry Association received a telegram from the Xi'an Cigarette Industry Association in Shaanxi Province, stating that the Shaanxi Provincial Government has heavily imposed a 40% surtax, making it unbearable. They requested assistance, so a representative, Mr. Li Xinle, arrived in Shanghai on the 3rd and immediately went to the Cigarette Manufacturers Association. He was received by Chairman Shen Weiting. Representative Li explained his purpose and requested prompt assistance in sending telegrams to various parties, requesting that the 40% surtax be cancelled. Chairman Shen immediately agreed to send telegrams to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and the Ministry of Finance's Tax Bureau, requesting the cancellation of the tax. The representative was satisfied and left to return to Shaanxi to report back. The association yesterday sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance and the Tax Bureau, requesting that they forward a letter to the Shaanxi Provincial Government to quickly cancel the surtax to alleviate the difficulties faced by businesses. The details are as follows:

Telegram to the Tax Bureau

The Shanghai Cigarette Manufacturers Association, in response to a telegram from the Shaanxi Tobacco Industry and the request from representative Li, telegraphed the Ministry of Finance's Tax Bureau yesterday, stating: "Respectfully informing, we recently received a telegram from the Xi'an Cigarette Industry Association, which said, 'To the Shanghai Cigarette Industry Association, the Shaanxi government is heavily imposing a 40% surtax, which exceeds the regular tax by 64 yuan for Grade 1 cigarettes and 32 yuan for Grade 2 cigarettes, causing business to be sluggish and hardship to be extreme. Such a heavy tax burden is unsustainable. Therefore, we have sent Mr. Li Xinle as a representative to present our case, and we respectfully request your consideration and ask the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce to jointly assist in petitioning the Ministry of Finance to order the reduction or exemption of the surtax in order to comply with the central tax regulations, thereby alleviating our suffering and maintaining the status quo. Respectfully awaiting your reply.' The Xi'an Cigarette Industry Association bows eastward," and so on. We have found that once cigarettes have paid the unified tax, they can be circulated domestically. Now, the Shaanxi Provincial Government is heavily imposing a 40% tobacco tax, which is actually a violation of the unified tax regulations. Businesses are struggling and cannot withstand the burden. Therefore, we are writing to your bureau, requesting that you promptly send a letter to the Shaanxi Provincial Government to cancel the heavy tax imposition as soon as possible, in order to maintain tax revenue and alleviate the difficulties of businesses. (Omitted) We extend our public friendship to the Ministry of Finance's Tax Bureau."

Letter to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce

"Respectfully informing, we recently received a telegram from the Xi'an Cigarette Industry Association (original telegram omitted above), and so on. We have found that once cigarettes have paid the unified tax, they can be circulated domestically. Now, the Shaanxi Provincial Government is heavily imposing a 40% tobacco tax, which is actually a violation of the unified tax regulations. Businesses are struggling and cannot withstand the burden. In addition to writing to the Ministry of Finance's Tax Bureau, requesting that they send a letter to the Shaanxi Provincial Government to cancel the heavy tax imposition as soon as possible, in order to maintain tax revenue and alleviate the difficulties of businesses, we are writing to your chamber, respectfully requesting that you consider the plight of businesses and promptly send a telegram to the Shaanxi Provincial Government, requesting that they allow the cancellation of the heavy tax imposition as soon as possible, in order to lighten the burden and maintain business. We extend our public friendship to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce."

Telegram to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce yesterday sent a telegram to Shao Lizhi, Chairman of the Shaanxi Provincial Government, requesting the abolition of the heavily imposed cigarette surtax in Shaanxi Province. The original text is as follows: "To Chairman Shao Lizhi of the Shaanxi Provincial Government, on the 5th of this month, we received a letter from the Chinese Cigarette Manufacturers Association, stating that they had received a telegram from the Xi'an Cigarette Industry Association, which said, 'The Shaanxi government is imposing a 40% surtax, which exceeds the regular tax by 64 yuan for Grade 1 cigarettes and 32 yuan for Grade 2 cigarettes, causing business to be sluggish and hardship to be extreme. Such a heavy burden is unsustainable,' and so on. After deliberation, we have found that once cigarettes have paid the unified tax, they can be circulated domestically. Now, the Shaanxi Provincial Government is heavily imposing a 40% tobacco tax, which is actually a violation of the unified tax regulations. Businesses are struggling and cannot withstand the burden. In addition to writing to the Ministry of Finance's Tax Bureau, requesting that they send a letter to the Shaanxi Provincial Government to cancel the heavy tax imposition as soon as possible, in order to maintain tax revenue and alleviate the difficulties of businesses, we are writing to your chamber, respectfully requesting that you consider the plight of businesses and promptly send a telegram to the Shaanxi Provincial Government, requesting that they allow the cancellation of the heavy tax imposition as soon as possible, in order to lighten the burden and maintain business. We extend our public friendship, etc.' After the meeting, it was found that under the current unified tax system, all products from each factory, after paying the unified tax according to regulations when they leave the factory, can circulate throughout the country without being taxed again. Various provinces have separately added surtaxes under the name of local taxes, which have been repeatedly prohibited by ministerial documents and published in the Ministry of Finance's Tax Gazette. Your province has many things to be done, and tax revenue is insufficient, which is also well known to our chamber. However, according to the aforementioned situation, the Shaanxi tax surcharge is extremely heavy, and businesses cannot bear it. Although cigarettes are consumable goods, they are also under the umbrella of the national unified tax system, and the treatment should not be too different. Moreover, the cigarette unified tax is a major source of income for the national treasury, and the source of tax revenue should also be taken care of. In addition, the livelihood of the factory workers is also a concern, which should be taken into account. We hope that you will carefully consider how to balance the situation so that manufacturers in Shanghai can have a chance to catch their breath. We sincerely hope that you will grant us your full consideration and properly handle the matter. We would be extremely grateful. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce bows in song."

Shanghai Bar Association Fetes Mr. Escarra

Advocates Adopting Laws Based on Justice and Reason

Last night, the Shanghai Bar Association hosted a banquet at the Shipping Club on Guangdong Road in the Public Concession for Mr. Escarra (transliteration), a Frenchman and former member of the Beijing Law Codification Committee who was recommended by the League of Nations as a legal advisor to the National Government. New Minister of Justice Ju Juesheng, his specially appointed secretary Hu Chishan, and Zhang Yaozeng, Dong Kang, Li Shirui, Sun Zuji, and others were also invited. All members, including standing committee members Shen Junru, Chen Tingrui, and Wang Weizhen, executive supervisors Yan Yinwu, Hu Jue, Li Ming, Wu Kaisheng, Zhu Fuju, Yang Zhihao, Zhou Xiaoan, Zhang Zhengxue, Guo Shouyi, and Ma Junshuo, warmly received the guests. The party entered at seven o'clock, and the atmosphere was filled with toasts and lively conversation. During the banquet, the guests discussed the state of the judicial system in China. The gathering ended around nine o'clock, with both hosts and guests thoroughly satisfied. Excerpts from the speeches given by standing committee member Shen Junru and Mr. Escarra are as follows: (1) Standing committee member Shen said, "Today, our association is hosting a banquet for Mr. Escarra. We are very honored to have Mr. Escarra grace us with his presence. Mr. Escarra has studied Chinese characters and ancient Chinese jurists, and he holds our ancient laws in particularly high regard. However, many of those in our country who discuss law often disregard our traditions. Now, the Lawyers Association of the Republic of China has discovered the Chinese legal system, and Mr. Escarra happens to be a scholar of ancient Chinese law. He can be considered a pioneer of overseas research in this area. We are very fortunate that Mr. Escarra will soon contribute his research findings to the world." (2) Mr. Escarra said in his speech, "I am very grateful to the Shanghai Bar Association for this banquet today. Since 1924, I have been helping China in a very simple way as an advisor. I have great respect and affection for China. China is a vast and resource-rich country. I believe that the creation of a new society through the compilation of modern legal codes requires careful observation to ensure they are truly applicable. I hope that the doctrines of Confucius will still be incorporated in modern laws, which may conflict with Roman law. There is no such drawback to adopting laws based on justice and reason. If there are matters that cannot be reconciled, there are interpretive systems that can be used to remedy them. I hope that your association will continue its efforts in the field of law. I wish you all good health." Zhang Yaozeng, Wu Kaisheng, Li Shirui, and others also gave speeches, which are omitted for brevity.

Five Gunshots Fired at Zhoujiaqiao in Western Shanghai

Zhu Xingtai's Home Robbed

One Thief, Wang A'san, Captured

Zhu Xingtai, a 53-year-old man from Changzhou, residing at No. 2358 Jeesfeer Road, Zhoujiaqiao, in western Shanghai, runs a reed mat shop and has some savings. Around 8 p.m. the night before last, Zhu had just finished dinner when three thugs suddenly broke into his home. Two of them wielded handguns, creating a menacing atmosphere and forbidding anyone to make a sound. Zhu, realizing that they were robbers, ran outside and shouted for help to catch the thieves. The thugs, seeing that things were not going well, fired five shots with their handguns, but fortunately no one was injured. At that moment, Liu Guoshu, an officer from the Caojiadu Public Security Bureau, was patrolling the area with his colleagues when he heard the alarm. They rushed to the scene and bravely fought to arrest the thugs. One of them was apprehended on the spot, and two spent cartridges were also recovered. They were immediately taken back to the bureau. After Bureau Chief Wang Dasui interrogated them, the plaintiff, Zhu Xingtai, provided a statement of the previous events. The captured thug identified himself as Wang A'san, a 29-year-old man from Yancheng, residing on Xinmin Road in Zhabei. He stated that he and the two fugitives had gone to Zhu's house, not to rob, but because someone surnamed Liu had a deep grudge against Zhu and instructed them to go there with guns to assassinate him, which is why they failed to hit him. After obtaining the confession, the bureau chief ordered them to be held for further investigation and interrogation.

Funeral Committee for Patriotic Martyr Pan Hongsheng Sets Date for Funeral

Shanghai South Defense Corps Fourth Team Decides to Participate

Assigning Duties and Soliciting Donations from Hu Wenhu

The Funeral Committee for Patriotic Martyr Pan Hongsheng, organized by various circles in Shanghai, held its third funeral meeting at 2 p.m. yesterday. More than twenty people attended, including Zhang Yichen, Hu Fengxiang, Zhang Xianfang, Xu Yunhui, Qu Zhenhua, Chen Jiufeng, Zheng Dongshan, and Zhu Zhichun. (8) Funeral paraphernalia were discussed and then the meeting adjourned.

Continued Donations

Yesterday's continued donations from various sectors included: Wang Hao'an, ten yuan; Cotton Trading Association, ten yuan; Chinese Securities Exchange, ten yuan; Hardware Association, ten yuan; Qu Zhenhua raised fifty yuan from twenty-eight households; Gongda Rice Store, five yuan; Wang Jingdong raised seventeen yuan, and donated thirteen yuan himself; Wei Langxuan, five yuan; Renfeng Dyeing and Weaving Factory, one bolt of white cloth. Yesterday's donation of one hundred yuan from China National Goods Company was a mistake and should have been The Shanghai National Goods Company and is hereby corrected.

Letter to Orphanage

The Committee yesterday sent a letter to the Orphanage and the Postal Workers' Union, requesting that all Boy Scouts participate in the funeral of Martyr Pan on the day of the funeral. The original letter stated, "Respectfully informing, the funeral of patriotic martyr Pan Hongsheng is scheduled for 12 noon on the 11th of this month. We request that your association/institution provide the military band, Boy Scouts, and bicycle team to lead the procession. We would be grateful if you could attend at that time to comfort the spirit of the martyr. We have appointed Committee Member Yu Yaoqiu to liaise with you. We hope you will take note of this matter."

Letter to Hu Wenhu

The Committee sent a letter to overseas Chinese leader Hu Wenhu yesterday, saying, "Mr. Wenhu, we have long admired your charitable heart and enthusiasm for public welfare. We were honored to witness your presence in Shanghai during the recent festival. Your excellent reputation is universally admired, and we wish you good health and longevity. Respectfully informing, since the September 18th Incident, various sectors of society have been stirred by righteous indignation and have risen up to participate in the nation-saving movement. During the January 28th Incident, they joined the citizens' volunteer army, fought on the front lines, and engaged in passive resistance after the settlement by warning unscrupulous merchants and sacrificing everything to demonstrate the spirit of our nation. Members of the Patriotic Martyr Society, including Pan Hongsheng, were arrested and subjected to torture to extract confessions, resulting in internal injuries. They were released on bail in critical condition, but medical treatment was ineffective, and he passed away at 5 a.m. on the 3rd of this month. Our association mourns the martyr's loyalty to the country and his commitment to the public good. His work remains unfinished, which cannot but make us sad. The martyr's family includes an elderly mother with white hair and a blind elderly father, and they are destitute. In order to commend his honor in life and grief in death, the association has established a funeral committee to handle his funeral and burial and provide for his family, and to erect a monument for a public burial to express our sorrow and commemorate him. This is a major undertaking that requires a great deal of funds. Therefore, we have appointed Chen Binghui and Chen Jiufeng as representatives to visit you. We hope that you will grant us an audience and provide guidance. We know that you are a leader in the industry and will surely appreciate the meaning of saving the country through domestic goods, support the patriotic movement, commend the martyr, and contribute generously to comfort his soul and encourage those who come after him. We are deeply moved and hopeful. We respectfully inform you of this matter and wish you well."

The Wu Futang Descendants' Sisters-in-Law Resolve Property Dispute

Appeal Permitted to Be Withdrawn

Following the successive deaths of Wu Xingsheng and Wu Meisheng, brothers and descendants of the deceased shareholder Wu Futang of Ruikang Paint Shop, their sisters-in-law, Wu Xu and Wu Bao, engaged in litigation in the First Special District Local Court over the inheritance of over two million in ancestral property. According to Wu Xu's petition, all of the ancestral property was in Wu Bao's possession, and she requested a judgment ordering Wu Bao to hand it over for equal distribution. However, Wu Bao countered, arguing that Wu Xu was merely a concubine of Xingsheng and had no children, thus lacking the standing to contest the inheritance. Furthermore, Xingsheng had been dead for fourteen years, and the statute of limitations had long expired. Following the initial trial by the court, it was determined that the plaintiff, Wu Xu, had no grounds for her lawsuit, and the case was dismissed. Wu Xu, dissatisfied with the judgment, retained lawyers Zhang Shizhao and Peng Yuanxun to appeal to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. She presented various reasons for disagreeing with the original judgment, citing legal precedents to support Wu Xu's right to demand a share of the inheritance, and requested the reversal of the original judgment. The Second Branch of the High Court, upon receiving the appeal, summoned both parties for questioning and advised them to seek an out-of-court settlement to avoid prolonged litigation. The parties have now reached an agreement through the mediation of relatives. The appellant, Wu Xu, has accepted the terms of the settlement and abandoned her claims. Yesterday afternoon, the scheduled date for the continued hearing, her lawyers Zhang Shizhao and Peng Yuanxun appeared in court and declared the circumstances of the out-of-court settlement, requesting permission to withdraw the appeal. Presiding Judge Li Dong approved the request, bringing the case to a close.

New Life Hospital's Morphine Production Case Adjudicated

Individual Sentences Handed Down

Qian Baiyan, also known as Mian, a doctor from Zhenjiang, age twenty-five, established the New Life Hospital at 799-801 Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession. He secretly partnered with Zhang Sen, a Ningbo native currently at large, to set up a morphine production operation in the vacant second and third floors of the hospital. They illicitly manufactured and sold morphine, reaping substantial profits. On the morning of the fifth of last month at nine o'clock, French police officers, including Chief Inspector Lambert, Inspector Li Yaolong, Detective Zhang Daorong, and patrolmen Liu Jinrong and Shen Jinshu, discovered the operation and raided the premises. They confiscated manufacturing equipment and arrested Qian, along with accomplices Lu Xianglong, Li Asan, Yang Xing, and suspects Zhang Jinfu, Zhu Huaming, and Zhang Ziwei, totaling seven individuals. They were handed over to the Second Special District Court. The police lawyer prosecuted them under Article 6 of the Anti-Opium Law for manufacturing narcotics. The details of the trial have been reported in previous newspapers. The case has now concluded its inquiry. Yesterday morning at ten o'clock, Presiding Judge Wang Gangxu presided over the First Criminal Court and ordered the defendants to be brought to court. Qian Xiangyan was sentenced to two years' imprisonment and fined one thousand yuan for assisting in the manufacture of opium substitutes. Lu Xianglong was sentenced to two years' imprisonment and fined eight hundred yuan for assisting in the manufacture of opium substitutes. Li Asan and Yang Xing were each sentenced to one year and six months' imprisonment for assisting in the manufacture of opium substitutes. Zhang Jinfu, Zhu Huaming, and Zhang Ziwei were found not guilty. During the appeal period, Qian, Lu, Li, and Yang were remanded to the detention center. Zhang, Zhu, and Zhang, who were acquitted, were required to provide a three thousand yuan bail, guaranteed by a shop, to ensure their availability for future summons. Qian Baiyan's defense lawyer stated that Qian was currently detained in the hospital and had various matters that still needed to be settled. He also requested permission for bail. The judge stated that a cash bail of fifteen thousand yuan was required for him to be released on bail. After the announcement, the police escorted the defendants back to detention.

Old Painter Accused

Li Xiujin Files Suit for Abandonment

Old Painter Absent Due to Illness

Cheng Yaosheng, also known as Dezhang, a renowned calligrapher and painter from Anhui, once enjoyed great prestige. His fees for each fan painting would reach tens of gold coins. Now approaching seventy years of age and blind in both eyes, and possessing considerable wealth, he abandoned his career in calligraphy and painting and rented a residence at No. 9 South Anli, Xinzha Road. Recently, however, Li Xiujin (age eighteen), a woman from Changzhou, filed a lawsuit in the First Special District Criminal Court, accusing Cheng of abandonment. The substance of her complaint was that at the age of seventeen, she was introduced to Cheng as his wife by Yang Ren, a colleague of Cheng's from the Jiheng Pawnshop in Changzhou. They initially resided in places such as Muqiaotou in Changzhou. The following year, she gave birth to a son named Rongguan, who soon died. Subsequently, Cheng accompanied the plaintiff to Shanghai, where he pursued calligraphy and painting. However, the couple's relationship deteriorated, and when the plaintiff was thirty-three years old, Cheng engaged in illicit relations with a Wuxi maidservant, openly cohabiting with her at home. As a result, the plaintiff was subjected to beatings and abuse. To protect her life, she separated from Cheng and temporarily resided at the Guangfu Temple on West Heng Street in Changzhou. This has been the case for over ten years. Initially, Cheng provided some expenses, but for the past five years, he has not provided any living expenses. The plaintiff sent a letter of inquiry, but Cheng denied that she was his wife and demanded proof. Therefore, she filed a lawsuit requesting that he be punished under Article 310 of the Criminal Code for abandonment and demanding that Cheng, who possesses assets of hundreds of thousands of yuan, provide her with a one-time payment of fifty thousand yuan. The Special District Court approved the lawsuit. Yesterday morning, Presiding Judge Feng Shide opened the First Criminal Court to conduct the hearing. The defendant, Cheng Yaosheng, was absent and was represented by lawyer Ma Nangeng, who stated that Cheng was unable to attend court due to illness and that a settlement of the case was possible, so he requested a postponement. The court questioned Li Xiujin about the events. She testified as described above, adding that the defendant now denies that she is his wife. In addition to the original matchmaker Yang Rensheng, there were wedding invitations at the time which are being sought from her hometown. When residing in Yongnianli, Baker Road, famous painters Wang Yiting, Zheng Xiaoxu, and Wang Yiting's son Shaomei often came to visit and could be called as witnesses. Judge Feng, noting the defendant's absence, ruled that the case could not proceed and adjourned the hearing to a later date.

Special District Rickshaw Merchants Petition the Municipal Council; Reply Given Yesterday

Merchants Dissatisfied; to Petition Again Today

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, rickshaw merchants in the Special District, protesting the illegal and excessive fines imposed by the Rickshaw Committee, the violation of Chinese law by forcing rickshaw pullers to register, and the compulsion to replace rickshaws with new models, petitioned the Municipal Council the day before yesterday. The authorities instructed them to await a response yesterday. Therefore, representatives Jin Chunlin, Wang Kun, Qiu Jilang, Shi Shaoan, Hua Zhongfeng, Bao Zhenhuang, Zhao Rongfu, Lu Yuzhai, Yin Zhifang, Wang Runtao, and others, totaling ten individuals, went to the Municipal Council at ten o'clock in the morning. They were again received by He De Kui, the Director. He De Kui replied with the following: (1) The Municipal Council will first test the new regulations on rickshaw owners. If the results are unsatisfactory, modifications will be considered. (2) Efforts will be made to allow the continued use of existing old-style rickshaw bodies. At four o'clock in the afternoon, the rickshaw merchants of the Special District held another temporary meeting, attended by over three hundred people. Chairman Jin Chunlin reported the results of the petition. After discussion, it was generally agreed that the replacement of rickshaw models and the registration of rickshaw pullers violated the resolutions of the Board of Directors and the approval of the Equal Rights Association. In order to respect the Municipal Council's position, the rickshaw merchants decided to acknowledge the validity of the resolutions. They stated that they would continue to oppose the Rickshaw Committee if it disregarded the hardships of rickshaw owners and pullers. As a result, ten representatives were selected to report to the Municipal Council and petition again today.

Record of the Second Board Meeting of the Gaoqiao Rural Improvement Association

Pilot Project in the Xingang Experimental Zone

Loan Program and Cooperatives

The Shanghai Gaoqiao Rural Improvement Association held its second board meeting yesterday (October 5th) at noon at the Local Association on Jing'an Temple Road. Board members Pan Hongding, Zhong Yuliang, Yang Weiyu, Su Shude, Qu Shao Yi Huang Renzhi, Liu Zhanen, and Zhang Wei were present. President and Chairman of the Board Du Yuesheng was absent due to other matters and was represented by Mr. Huang Renzhi. First, Director-General Wang Kui Sheng reported on the actual work situation of the previous month as follows: (1) the opening of the Gaoqiao Township Public Education Implementation Site and its future work plan, (2) the process of selecting Xingang as the experimental zone, (3) the recent recruitment of two female trainees to join the work, both local young women with considerable education and committed to serving rural women, (4) the reception of local youth and the invitation of Mr. Zou Bingwen, Director of the Agricultural Department of the Shanghai Bank, to Gaoqiao for inspection, and the process of preparing for credit loans and organizing cooperatives. Chairman Huang Renzhi and the board members expressed their appreciation for the active work of the staff and hoped for continued efforts. Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association Cables Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to Strictly Prohibit Grave Robbing

To Curb Banditry and Secure the Homeland

The Ningbo Sojourners Association in Shanghai cabled Chairman Chiang Kai-shek at the Nanchang Headquarters yesterday, stating: "To Chairman Chiang Kai-shek of the Nanchang Headquarters, we have repeatedly received reports from fellow villagers in Yin County, Zhenhai, and other places, stating that recently, with the construction of roads and fortresses in these counties, workers from other provinces have entered the area in large numbers. Thugs have infiltrated among them, causing disturbances everywhere. These people move in and out of the mountains and forests, even taking advantage of people's unpreparedness to rob old and new graves. The local people, intimidated by their violence, dare not speak out and have no choice but to ask our association for assistance from afar. Therefore, we respectfully request you to immediately cable the military and political leaders in charge, strictly ordering their subordinates to earnestly restrain the workers, conduct thorough investigations, and punish offenders according to military law, in order to curb banditry and secure the homeland. We eagerly await your response. Yu Hede and others of the Ningbo Sojourners Association in Shanghai respectfully kowtow."

Record of Conversation with Mrs. Tao Aider, President of the American Red Cross

China Needs Peace and Time

Mrs. Tao Aider, President of the American Red Cross and Executive Committee Member of the China Child Welfare Association, arrived in Shanghai some days ago and has been warmly welcomed by various circles, as reported in the newspapers. Yesterday afternoon at four o'clock, Chen Zhengfan, an officer in the Education Group of the China Child Welfare Association, visited Mrs. Tao Aider at the Cathay Hotel for discussions. During the conversation, Mrs. Tao made the following remarks and requested that they be published in Shanghai newspapers:

I personally feel deeply ashamed and grateful for the generous treatment I have received from all parties during this visit to Shanghai. In Shanghai, I have many friends and relatives, and I am extremely pleased to have the opportunity to meet and converse with them. My husband, Mr. John Alan Tao Aider, was formerly the American Naval Attaché in China, and I resided in China with him for over twenty years. Therefore, I have a profound impression of China and a strong sense of connection. This time, revisiting this old place, I feel that everything has the atmosphere of flourishing, and China's child welfare事业, under the leadership of President Kong Xiangxi of the Child Welfare Association, is showing leaping progress. In the past few days, I have visited the Child Welfare Association's education and care home, nursery, clinic, and the activities organized by the Shanghai Children's Welfare Association, and I am very satisfied with them all. I firmly believe that the culture of any country depends on the footsteps of children, so I have a great interest and faith in the child welfare business of China and the United States. I deeply wish to contribute my meager efforts, bit by bit. The intellectual women of China have now stepped into a new stage, no longer confining their vision and energy to the small family sphere. It is a gratifying phenomenon that they also know to come out and serve the society and the country. The Shanghai YWCA and the Chinese Women's Temperance Association provide suitable dormitories for the general working women of Shanghai, with clean bedrooms, beautiful reception rooms, entertainment rooms, and reading rooms, offering comfort and safety, so that women who work far from home can enjoy the pleasure of feeling at home and avoid wasting money and adapting to the environment. Their contribution is so great that it is unnecessary to mention. What China needs most today is peace and time. All old ideas, old habits, and old systems that violate modernization must be destroyed one by one, and all new ideas, new habits, and new systems that are suitable for modernization must be built one by one. Then China can become a modern country and occupy a place on the modern world stage. The World Red Cross Conference held in Tokyo, Japan last month lasted for fourteen days, with representatives from the Red Cross Societies of sixty countries attending. The results were quite satisfactory. The next conference is scheduled to be held in Madrid, the capital of Spain, in 1938. I sincerely hope that the Chinese Red Cross can also send representatives to attend at that time.

They were all satisfied. From now on, the travel business in Southeast Asia will no longer be exclusively controlled by foreigners.

Shanghai Public Hospital to Be Managed by the City

The land on which the Shanghai Public Hospital in the Nanshi district is located is leased from the original grain storage base. The grain storage base is jointly owned by the city and county governments. Since the division of governance between the city and county, the hospital has been jointly managed by both. Currently, with the implementation of the division of jointly owned public property between the city and county, the Shanghai Public Hospital must also be resolved simultaneously. The Shanghai County Government proposed a swift and clear division to avoid prolonged indecision. The Shanghai Municipal Government has also expressed its agreement and has instructed the Finance, Public Works, Land, Social Affairs, and Health Bureaus, stating that the original grain storage funds and original public property should be divided together. However, since the Shanghai Hospital is related to the city's health business, it should be assigned to the city. Therefore, they are planning a reorganization to turn it into a city-run treatment facility, which will facilitate supervision and improvement to meet the medical needs of the citizens.

Social Bureau Suppresses Vagrants Extorting Under False Pretenses

Attention All Hat Stall Owners

Report to the Police If Encountered

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the Shanghai Social Bureau recently received a confidential report that Zhang Aiyun, Zhang Shenggen, Ge Chengyu, Ge Chengzun, and other unemployed vagrants are extorting 2.5 yuan from over one hundred hat stalls in the Chinese and French Concessions under the pretext of organizing a labor union. They have stipulated that the fee be collected twice a year, in spring and autumn. Those who refuse to comply are threatened with axes and iron rulers. Upon receiving the report, the bureau immediately dispatched personnel to investigate. Although Han Genbao, Ge Zengwu, Ge Chengyun, and others initiated the establishment of the Hat Washing Workers' United Benefit Association in December of the 21st year of the Republic, it was never registered with the Social Bureau and soon ceased to exist informally. However, the names of Zhang Aiyun, Zhang Shenggen, Ge Chengyu, and Ge Chengzun are not on the list of initiators of this association. Furthermore, there has been no recent organization of a hat washing workers' union. The bureau considers this situation to be a clear case of unemployed vagrants extorting money. In addition to strict suppression, all hat stalls are authorized to report to the police if they encounter the above-mentioned situations, so as to avoid being defrauded.

Page 12

Garment Shop Owner Dies Suddenly After Two Injections

Shop Assistants Hastily Summon Doctor

Obtained the Services of a Venereal Disease Specialist

Expired After a Noisy Fart

Wife Unsuccessful in Seeing Him Before His Death

Pan Jintao, age thirty-nine, a native of Nanhui, had been running the Qinyuji Garment Shop at No. 212 Route Paul Beau in the French Concession for many years. The business was quite prosperous. Unexpectedly, Pan suddenly suffered from dizziness within the past two or three days, recurring intermittently. He thought it was a minor ailment and did not rush to seek medical treatment. On the afternoon of the fifth, at 1:30 PM, Pan's illness recurred in the shop. He felt dizzy and unable to stand up, so he went to the room to lie down and rest. However, he suddenly fell to the ground before reaching the bed. The shop assistants, upon learning of this, rushed to help him up and carried him to bed. He immediately became delirious and unconscious. His wife, Shi, happened to be out on business. The shop assistants and residents were in a panic and immediately summoned a doctor, without taking the time to choose carefully. Since they had a telephone installed, they checked the telephone directory and found Shude Hospital at No. 180 Balizhao Street, a specialist in venereal diseases and gynecology. They called the hospital and summoned Dr. Gu Zongwen (age forty, from Wuxi), the director. Gu, without delay, immediately hired a Xiang Sheng taxi according to standard rates and rushed to the clinic. At this time, the patient was barely breathing and his pulse was extremely weak. Without asking for the consent of the patient's family, Gu administered an injection of coramine, a cardiac stimulant, into his arm. It had no effect. He then administered a second injection into the patient's chest. The patient let out a gasp, and as the needle was withdrawn, a noisy fart was released from below. The patient then breathed his last breath and passed away. Gu then charged his family for medical expenses, taxi fare, and a registration fee, totaling 27.8 yuan. At this time, Pan's wife had not yet returned to the shop. No one in the shop was responsible for this medical expense, and Gu was urgently demanding payment. While he was pressing for payment, Pan's wife, Shi, returned from outside and saw that her husband had died. She heard from neighbors and residents that Gu had been careless and caused his death. She immediately reported to the French police, who dispatched Chinese and Western detectives to investigate and took the two medicine bottles as evidence. The body was then transported by vehicle to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Mortuary for an autopsy. Yesterday, the Second Special District Court was notified and appointed Prosecutor Wang Ren, along with forensic doctors Wei and Jiang, and clerk Peng, to visit the mortuary at noon to examine the body. After examining the body, they took their seats and questioned Pan Shi, the deceased's wife, Dr. Gu Zongwen, the defendant, and Xiao Zhou, the maidservant, about the circumstances of the illness, injections, and medical treatment. They concluded that Pan Jintao had died of illness. The body was handed over to his wife for burial.

Yixing Girl Zhao Jinfeng Jumps Out of a Water Pit

Unable to Bear the Abuse of a Brothel Keeper

Seeking Relief from the Public Security Bureau

Zhao Jinfeng, a girl from Yixing, is 16 years old and quite beautiful. She used to live with her mother in her hometown, making a living by farming. Last April, due to the bankruptcy of the rural area and poor harvests in the fields, which led to economic hardship and difficult living conditions, the girl was lured to Shanghai by a rogue neighbor under the guise of introducing her to work in a factory as a female worker. She was sold into prostitution at the Xing surname brothel across from the Changxing Inn on Xixin Bridge in the French Concession. Every night, the brothel keeper forced her to go to small inns to receive guests and engage in prostitution, subjecting her to trampling. Moreover, the brothel keeper was of a shrewish nature. If Zhao Girl slightly disobeyed her, she would be whipped and even deprived of food and drink. All kinds of abuse made it no different from a human hell. At that time, the girl thought of running away many times, but in the end, because the brothel keeper and others kept a close watch, and she had no relatives or friends in Shanghai to turn to for help, she had to endure the humiliation with pain. Unexpectedly, recently the brothel keeper's abuse of Zhao Girl has been even worse than before, causing Zhao Girl to be unable to bear it any longer. Yesterday at around 8:00 AM, she fled with another private prostitute named Zheng Xifu and threw herself into the outer road police station of the 16th Pupu Branch of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, asking for relief. When Chief Jin interrogated her about the case, Ms. Cai said that she was sixteen years old from a poor family. She was abducted to Shanghai as a child and raised as an adopted daughter in a private household of a certain surname in Daren Lane. Therefore, she did not know the surname and name of her biological parents. Last summer, when her body first showed unusual signs, she was forced by the brothel keeper to receive guests and suffered great humiliation. This time, she escaped specifically because she could not bear the brothel keeper's abuse and the life of a sacred female and asked for relief. The police chief ordered that a document be prepared to send the pair of pitiful young girls to the bureau together to find a way to help them.

Seeking Divorce After One Year of Marriage

Chen Dajun, a student at Fudan University from Dinghai, Zhejiang, is 23 years old and lives at No. 434 Xinmin Village, Maming Road, Bailainei, French Concession. He has recently been teaching at a Westerner's house. Last year, he developed love with Feng Heqing, a student at Moore Memorial Girls' School from Guangdong (21 years old this year, residing at No. 54 Dekang Lane, Fusheng Road, Zhabei), first through friendship, then got engaged. They got married last April 15th at Moore Memorial Church because both were Christians. Their love was as close as glue. In December, a son was born. Unexpectedly, flowers do not always bloom, and the moon is not always full. In September this year, they suddenly had disagreements, which were incompatible as water and milk. Feng Heqing hired a lawyer to file a petition with the civil court of the Second Special Court, requesting mediation for divorce and ordering the payment of alimony. Yesterday at around 10:00 AM, Judge Li Liang visited the Civil Seventh Court to summon both parties to the case for mediation. The petitioner's lawyer arrived on her behalf, stating the intention of the petition, and said that the respondent had insulted and scolded the petitioner not long after the marriage. As the petitioner had an elderly mother with no one to take care of her, and the petitioner lived with her mother, the respondent strongly opposed it. Therefore, the feelings of both parties were even more broken. In addition to requesting mediation for divorce, she also ordered the respondent to pay 2,000 yuan in alimony, which must be paid in one lump sum, as well as 100 yuan per month for living expenses and 50 yuan per month for child support. Chen Dajun, the respondent, said that after the marriage, the feelings between husband and wife were quite good. It was actually just an occasional quarrel and he did not want a divorce. After verifying the words, the court announced that the mediation had failed and ordered a formal lawsuit to be filed separately.

Case of Young Woman Shot on Hobilan Road

Local Court Hears Case Yesterday

Gu Yinzhen (i.e., Jin Gu's), a local young woman, lives at No. 25 Chenjiazhai, Caojiadu, West Shanghai, and works in a yarn factory. At around 5:00 AM on September 19th of this year, on her way to the factory, she was threatened by robbers with guns on Hobilan Road. She was forcibly robbed of two gold rings and they attempted to flee. Yinzhen was reluctant to give them up and chased after them. She was shot and injured by the robber. Afterwards, Gu Yinzhen reported to the Zhoujiaqiao police station to arrest them, but they were not caught. Later, Yinzhen accused Jin Bosun, the cousin of her husband, of being the perpetrator and requested that he be brought to justice. Prosecutor Wu Deying arrested Jin Bosun and took his statement. He was detained pending further investigation. It is reported that Prosecutor Wu Deying has clearly investigated this case and filed charges with the criminal court. Yesterday morning, Chief Judge Liu Enrong opened the Third Court to hear the case and ordered Jin Bosun to be brought to the case. (Question) What is your relationship with Jin Zhuqing? (Answer) Paternal Uncle. (Question) What is your relationship with Jin Jinsheng? (Answer) Paternal cousin, the same age. (Question) Who is Gu Yinzhen? (Answer) Jin Jinsheng's wife. (Question) That day, you shot your cousin-in-law? (Answer) I was wronged. That day, I was working at the Sino-Foreign Bookstore. (Question) Where is the Sino-Foreign Bookstore? (Answer) No. 90, at the intersection of Luban Road and Lafayette Road in the French Concession. (Question) You said you were working in the bookstore. What evidence do you have? (Answer) Please ask the court to investigate Xue Quansheng, the director of the typesetting room, or ask the manager. (Question) Can you go out casually in your store? (Answer) No, if you have something to leave the store, you must report to the manager and get permission with a written note. And the store was very busy that day, with day and night shifts. (Question) What hatred do you have with Jin Jinsheng? (Answer) Because Yang Rongkang sold the land, my father Jin Jieqing, and Jin Jinsheng's father Zhuqing, and Wang Xiaomao, Chen Heshang, etc. acted as intermediaries. Because the intermediary fee was not available, Zhuqing borrowed money from my father and was refused, so he framed me. (Question) Why didn't you give the intermediary fee? (Answer) Because Yang Rong went bankrupt, so he didn't give it. (Question) Any other opinions? (Answer) No. (Question) Why did your father sue Jin Yinxiang (Jin Bosun's cousin-in-law), etc.? (Answer) Because they colluded to beat my father, and later they were persuaded to disperse by the villagers. (Question) Since it was already over, why did you shoot her with a gun? (Answer) Jin Zhuqing borrowed money from my father and was refused, so he falsely accused me. (Question) Is there any definite evidence to present? (Answer) When the money was borrowed, Jin Yushi was present. Next, according to Jin Gu's (Gu Yinzhen), 21 years old, (Question) Is your injury healed? (Answer) Not healed. (Question) How many injuries are there? (Answer) There are two injuries. (Question) What day were you injured? (Answer) Around 5:40 AM on the 12th of the lunar eighth month. (Question) Where were you injured? (Answer) On You'nigang Road. (Question) Where were you going? (Answer) The Star Yarn Factory. (Question) Who injured you? (Answer) Jin Bosun. (Question) He is your relative. How could he shoot you with a gun? (Answer) Last year, he and we got married on the same day at the Catholic Church and fought over the order of precedence. (Question) Would this small thing cause you to be shot with a gun? (Answer) Face is involved, he bears a grudge. (Question) Did you see clearly that he shot the gun? (Answer) He chased after me on a bicycle and painted ink on his face when he committed the crime. (Question) Who was in front? (Answer) Jin Bosun was in front. (Question) Where did the bullet enter? (Answer) In the back of my heart. (Question) How many shots were fired? (Answer) Four shots, the first two bullets missed. (Question) What happened after the shooting? (Answer) At that time, I fainted on the ground and was robbed of two gold rings and fled. (Question) Why did he rob you after shooting you down? (Answer) To cover up people's eyes and ears. (Question) What did you look like when you fell to the ground after being shot? (Answer) Face down. (Question) Who reported the news to your home? (Answer) A person living in Majiajiao whose name I don't know. (Question) Why didn't you report to the police station in charge at that time and send the injury to this court for examination? (Answer) Because I was unconscious, etc. Finally, according to Jin Zhuqing, 37 years old, farmer, (Question) Who is Ms. Gu to you? (Answer) Daughter-in-law. (Question) Do you know that your daughter-in-law was shot and injured? (Answer) Shi A'si came to report the news. (Question) When did he tell you? (Answer) Around 6:00 AM. (Question) What is your relationship with Shi? (Answer) Best friends. (Question) How was your daughter-in-law lying on the ground? (Answer) Lying face down, unconscious. (Question) What did you do after you arrived? (Answer) I immediately sent my daughter-in-law to the hospital and reported to the patrol house there (Jing'an Temple). (Question) Did the patrol house send someone? (Answer) A Westerner, five Chinese policemen, and they took my son Jin Sheng to the patrol house to inquire about the situation. (Question) The next day, the newspaper reported that your daughter-in-law was shot by a man in his thirties wearing a blue cloth short coat and pants. (Answer) I didn't publish it. (Question) Why didn't you report to the Zhoujiaqiao police station at that time? (Answer) I didn't go to report. (Question) Why did you tell me after five or six days? (Answer) Because my daughter-in-law was unconscious. (Question) Jin Bosun said that you borrowed money from his father and framed him out of hatred. (Answer) That is not the case. (Question) When you borrowed money from Jin Bosun's father Jieqing, was anyone there to hear it? (Answer) Zhuqing's answer was vague. At this point in the interrogation, the lawyer Shi Liang, hired by the defendant, stated that the defendant was indeed wronged. The questioner said that this case needs to be investigated and adjourned for another day to summon the witness for further action. The defendant was remanded in custody.

Private Sale of Opium Sentenced

Wang Jinshou, a detective from the Jiaxing Road patrol house, saw Fujian native Lin Hongti and Yongren Zhang Alin in the Fuhuali Lane of Dongyouheng Road at 7:40 PM the day before yesterday. Finding their behavior suspicious, he intercepted them. He found 12 and a half taels of opium on Lin. He learned that the opium was brought to the location to be sold on behalf of Hong Achun, who was living at No. 71 in the lane. Detective Wang went to Hong's house to arrest him, but he was not there. He took Lin and Zhang, together with the opium, to the patrol house. The patrol head ordered them to be detained. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Criminal Third Court of the First Special District. Gongbu Ju lawyer Li Zhishan stated the previous situation and said that Zhang Alin had been dealt with for gambling on flower clubs before and asked for severe punishment. Then, Detective Wang reported the details of the solved case and presented the opium for inspection. After Judge Xiao Xiefei interrogated the two defendants and clarified the facts, he sentenced Lin Hongti to six months in prison, Zhang Alin to one year, and confiscated the opium.

Suzhou Elder Privately Carrying Red Pills

Fined Thirty Yuan

Chinese detective Liu Zhongcheng learned that someone was selling the poisonous drug red pills for profit in Zhaofeng Lane, Zhaofeng Road. He went secretly at 6:10 PM the day before yesterday and arrested an old man from Suzhou named Zhu Fujin. He found a small bag of red pills on him, totaling 500 pills. He took him, along with the evidence, to the Jiaxing Road patrol house and reported to the patrol head, who ordered him to be detained. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Criminal Third Court of the First Special Court. Gongbu Ju lawyer Li Zhishan stated what happened. At that time, the red pills were presented for inspection. When the defendant was questioned, he said that he was sweeping the lane in Zhaofeng Lane. The red pills were given to him by a fleeing woman named Gendi to take to a certain place in Zhabei. They were not his. He has an elderly mother at home who relies on him to live. He begged for leniency. Judge Wu Zehan sentenced Zhu Fujin to a fine of 30 yuan as a warning and confiscated the evidence.

Ferry Boats Compete for Business, Two Gangs Clash

The ferry boats that transport passengers of the Chongming steamship in Wusong were previously operated by Xu Fengshan Guanfu and other ten people from the Hakka gang. Recently, after the Chongming gang Zhu Xi and others came forward to operate it, they officially rented a house on the shore and hung up a sign to transport passengers, which caused Xu Fengshan from the Hakka gang to have no means of making a living. The day before yesterday afternoon, Xu and others gathered a crowd to clash with Zhu Xi. Both sides used force. The gang police were summoned to the Wusong police station. After questioning by Chief Fu, because the case involved business disputes, the police were ordered to report the two parties to the general office for decision.

Impersonating a Public Official Touching a Woman's Abdomen

Ni Junxiang is Cunning and Sent for Investigation

Fan Leng's, a 23-year-old woman from Pudong living at No. 25 Wangyi Ma Lane in the city, is six months pregnant with a large belly. At 6:30 PM the other day, she was walking through the bottom of the East Lane, as the lane was under construction and there were few pedestrians. Suddenly, three hooligans impersonating public officials searched for suspicious pedestrians in order to rob them of their property. Fan Leng's was stopped by them and searched. As she had no silver dollars on her, the hooligans stroked the area around her belly. She questioned them as to what they were touching. The hooligans said that they suspected she was pretending to be pregnant to smuggle red pills. Because she realized that the hooligans did not look like public officials, she grabbed one of them and shouted for the police. Zhang Chengfeng from Post 25 arrived to help and arrested two of them and took them to the Yimiao police station for investigation. After questioning by Chief Liu, the plaintiff stated the same as above. The defendants, Ni Junxiang, 30 years old, from Zhenjiang, and Liu Daquan, 24 years old, confessed that they did not impersonate public officials to search pedestrians. Because the plaintiff's belly was big and fun, they touched it for fun. Chief Liu believed that the defendant's confession was cunning and that they were actually searching under false pretenses and intending to rob property. They should be severely punished to respect the corrupting customs and sentenced to be sent to the general office for handling.

Verdict in the Case of Being Sued by the Times Daily

Lai Lansheng Fined Five Hundred Yuan

Xiang Kangyuan, an industrialist who runs the Kangyuan Canned Food Factory, has excellent business. However, recently, the Times Daily, a tabloid edited by Lai Lansheng, published an article on the 7th of last month, stating that Xiang Kangyuan was unable to maintain and closed down the Kangyuan Factory due to speculation in Japanese stocks. Xiang saw this and believed that the newspaper's report was completely a castle in the air, causing great damage to himself and the Kangyuan Factory. He sued Lai at the Xinzha patrol house. Attorney Qian Xunjiu of the Gongbu Ju Legal Department filed a public prosecution for defamation under Article 330 of the Criminal Law. The First Special Court had summoned him once. Lai Lansheng stated that in addition to apologizing to Mr. Xiang in major newspapers, he would also make corrections in this newspaper and write an impression record of the Kangyuan Factory, etc., for correction. Xiang said that since the defendant had made corrections, the private prosecution could not be filed, but Lai had to point out the contributor. After questioning by Judge Deng, he ordered Lai to pay 500 yuan to be released on bail pending judgment. Yesterday morning, Judge Deng Baosun opened the Criminal Second Court and announced the verdict. Lai Lansheng spread rumors and damaged the credit of others and was fined 500 yuan. If he commutes the imprisonment, it will be calculated at two yuan a day.

In October, the Shanghai Pushan Villa collected and buried 95 large coffins and 2,480 small coffins in the Chinese and French concessions in the north and south, and distributed 1,055 large and small coffins. Among them, the Villa collected 24 large coffins and 1,440 small coffins. In addition, the Xiqiao branch and various charitable halls in the French Concession collected 563 small coffins. Various patrol houses in the Public Concession collected 57 large coffins and 441 small coffins from abandoned infant corpses and unclaimed corpses from various hospitals within the boundary according to the notices. In addition, the Red Cross hospitals collected three large coffins, the Shanghai Epidemic Hospital collected one large coffin, the Shanghai Sanatorium collected one large coffin, the Tongren Hospital collected five large coffins, and the Lianyi Charity Society collected four large coffins and 36 small coffins. All the above corpses were collected by the Villa's vehicles and transported to the Yidi Cemetery in Dachang Tangqiao for burial and marked for collection. The White Cross Pushan Obstetrics Hospital on Xinmin Road, Zhabei, provided diagnosis and medicine to a total of 1,950 patients.

City News

Domestic OK Locks Sell Well Since foreign goods invaded our country's market, the spring door lock, which is a necessary device for the doors of upper-middle-class families in the past ten years, dates back to seventy or eighty years ago. It is known for its beauty and durability, and the keys have hundreds of thousands of different numbers. In recent years, Chinese people have also known how to set up factories to manufacture themselves, such as the OK brand of various spring door locks produced by Wanneng Factory, which is indeed better than imported ones. This is because the person in charge of the factory is brave in research and good at improvement, which makes the products more refined day by day. Moreover, the factory has always adhered to the principle of small profits, so the pricing is absolutely civilian-oriented, in order to benefit the public. It is found that the most common door lock currently used by our people sells for more than one yuan per piece, and the internal mechanism is almost the same, easy to pry open, and locking is equal to locking, thus creating a supreme opportunity for night owls. These losses are known to everyone who knows a little. Now, the factory has seen this and the selling price is only two yuan per piece, which is not comparable to foreign goods worth seven or eight yuan a piece. It is a waste of painstaking effort. Users are happy to buy OK locks because of their low price and good quality, and knowledge-minded people also believe that it is a domestic product and it is very necessary to promote it.

Xin Xin Rooftop Set Up Dove Raising Place Since the organization of the Homing Pigeon Association in this city, the number of pigeon raisers has increased day by day. Recently, Cai Ziwo, the director of the rooftop entertainment department of the Xin Xin Company on Nanjing Road, has specially set up a place on the rooftop to raise more than 100 pigeons. Every Saturday and Sunday, pigeon raising families gather on the rooftop to study each other. In the afternoon, the colorful pigeons of each family are released into the sky, thousands of them in groups, soaring and obscuring the eyes, which is enough to attract interest. This is also a unique way of playing games.
