Education News

Important News on the National Vocational School Labor Exhibition

The Ministry of Education is sponsoring the National Vocational School and Primary and Secondary School Labor Curriculum Achievement Exhibition, which is scheduled to open on December 1st at the Examination Yuan in Nanjing. During the current preparation period, the ten preparation personnel sent by the Ministry of Education are still handling the preparation matters concurrently in the Ministry. At present, various statistical charts are being drafted for the products that have been sent or reported to be sent from various provinces and cities, so that when the products from various provinces and cities are displayed, there will be a general chart from the Ministry of Education to guide the visitors to easily find what they are looking for. This work is extremely busy, and the staff members are currently cooperating in the division of labor. The Examination Yuan venue will not be completely vacated until the 15th of this month. From the 15th, the preparation personnel of the Ministry of Education will work with the representatives sent by the producers of various provinces and cities (Jiangxi has sent Lu Lianrui and Li Tanxi, Guangxi has sent Li Daneng, Hubei has sent Ma Shouxi, and Beiping has sent Qi Binru, etc., and there are still reports that representatives have been sent but have not yet arrived in Beijing) to the Examination Yuan venue to arrange the exhibition. Generally, remote provinces do not send representatives to Beijing to arrange the exhibition, but entrust friends in Beijing or staff members of the Ministry of Education to arrange the exhibition on their behalf. Many neighboring education departments have representatives arranging the exhibition themselves. Because the achievements of this session are divided into vocational schools and primary and secondary school labor courses, and the exhibition is organized by province and city, the provinces and cities must arrange it themselves. It is reported that all provinces and cities are participating, except for Guizhou, Xinjiang, and Qinghai, with a total of twenty-five provinces and cities. There are a total of thirty-odd thousand achievements. According to the current statistics of those who have reported or sent in, Weihaiwei has eleven categories (the following abbreviations are written in parentheses) and forty-seven items, Anhui (27) has three thousand two hundred and seventy-nine items, Shanxi (25) has nine hundred and fifty items, Yunnan (10) has one hundred and eighty-six items, Chahar (the number of items reported but not reported) Sichuan (14) has one hundred and thirty-two items, Gansu (nine categories, the number of items not reported) Ningxia (3) has twenty items, Suiyuan has one hundred and nineteen items, Guangxi has three hundred and seventy-two items, and the Twelfth Middle School has eight items, Shaanxi (22) has four hundred and thirty items, Beijing has two thousand one hundred and fifty items, Henan has forty tons (the number of items not reported) and Nanyang County has seven items, Qingdao (12) has about three hundred items, Nanjing (15 categories) has more than six hundred items, Hunan (20+) has 200+ boxes, Hebei (12) has two thousand items (including nine machines weighing about five tons), Shandong has one hundred boxes and three thousand items), Jiangsu (20) has three thousand six hundred and twenty-one items, Fujian (11 categories for vocational schools and 12 categories for primary and secondary schools) has a total of two thousand one hundred and fifty items, Hubei has more than one thousand items, Jiangxi has one thousand six hundred and odd items, Zhejiang has fifty boxes and three thousand items, Guangdong (12) has one hundred and twenty items, and Shanghai has about two thousand items. The above totals twenty-five provinces and cities and two schools, with a total of 31,700+ items, (excluding those from Cha, Gan, and the uncounted tonnage). Among them, four provinces and cities have more than three thousand items, six provinces and cities have more than two thousand items, three provinces and cities have more than one thousand items (including Shanxi with more than nine hundred items), four provinces and cities have more than three hundred items, and eight provinces and cities have less than three hundred items.

(Central News Agency, Kaifeng, 5th) Zhao Luan and Zhang Pishan of the Henan Education Department escorted the labor achievements of various schools to Beijing on the afternoon of the 5th to participate in the exhibition.

Military Education Requires On-Campus Residence

(Nanjing, 6th) The Directorate General of Military Training informed the Ministry of Education that many military instructors and assistant instructors of military science live off-campus, and there are also many who live outside freely, which causes many gaps in the relationship between teachers and students. It is now stipulated that all military instructors and military assistant instructors in each school must be ordered to reside on campus (they may live outside on the evening before the holidays). They must not live outside without the permission of the principal in order to set an example and hope to receive the same treatment as other teaching and administrative staff who reside on campus. The Ministry of Education yesterday issued an order to the education departments of all provinces and cities to inform all public and private high schools and above.

Approval of Subsidy for Zhongkai Agricultural School

(Nanjing, 6th) The Central Political Council approved a subsidy of 40,000 yuan for the Guangdong Private Zhongkai School of Agriculture and Engineering and designated it to be drawn from the second reserve fund for this year. The National Government has now ordered the Ministry of Finance to allocate it accordingly.

Hebei Schools to Begin Inspection of Military Training

(Tianjin, 5th) The Hebei National Military Training Committee has decided to inspect the military training of various schools separately starting this week. The first inspection was held at Beiyang Institute of Technology on the afternoon of the 5th, and the results were good.

Director Dai and Commissioner Sun of the Ministry of Education Inspect Shanghai Universities

The Ministry of Education sent Director Dai Xia and Commissioner Sun Guofeng to inspect the students in Shanghai universities. The work has been completed, and they returned to the Ministry yesterday. The reporter went to meet with Directors Dai and Sun to inquire about the inspection process. According to their account, the universities inspected in Shanghai this time were National Chiao Tung University, National Chinan University and its affiliated middle school and experimental school, National Tongji University and its affiliated senior high school and vocational school, National Shanghai Medical College, National Shanghai College of Commerce, Sino-French National Institute of Technology and its affiliated middle school, and China National University. A total of six national universities, five affiliated middle schools, vocational schools, and experimental schools of national universities, and one private school were inspected. Because the scope of each school was extensive or because there were many problems, the inspection took a little longer. We arrived in Shanghai on October 14th, and the next morning we met with Mr. Song Wusheng, a medical expert specially appointed by the Ministry of Education as a medical inspector. In the afternoon, we began the inspection. On the afternoon of the 15th and the 16th, we inspected the Sino-French National Institute of Technology and its affiliated middle school. On the 17th, we inspected the National Shanghai Medical College and Hospital with Mr. Song Wusheng. On the 18th, we inspected the teaching situation of various departments of the National Chiao Tung University. On the 19th, we inspected the equipment of various departments of the school. On the 20th, we inspected the administrative situation of various departments of the school. On the 22nd, we inspected the teaching and equipment situation of various departments of the National Chinan University. On the 23rd, we inspected the affiliated middle school and experimental school of the school. On the 24th, we inspected the administrative situation of various departments of the school. On the morning of the 25th, we inspected the Medical College of National Tongji University with Mr. Song Wusheng. In the afternoon, we inspected the teaching situation of the School of Engineering of the school. On the 26th, we inspected the equipment situation of the School of Engineering of the school. On the 27th, we inspected the hospital of the school with Mr. Song Wusheng. In the afternoon, we inspected the senior vocational school of the school. On the morning of the 29th, we inspected the affiliated middle school, the supplementary course, and the Wusong Public Health Area. In the afternoon, we inspected the administrative situation of various departments of the school. On the 30th, we inspected the China National University. On November 1st, we inspected the National Shanghai College of Commerce. On the 2nd, we sorted out the materials. On the 3rd, we returned to Beijing to report our mission. (Reporter's note: the 4th was Sunday, and we went to the Ministry to work on the 5th.) As for the scope of the inspection, in addition to the special issues that need to be carefully inspected according to the instructions of the textbooks, the organization of the administration of each school, the allocation of staff, their service spirit, the allocation of funds and their expenditure, the establishment of departments, the compilation and content of the curriculum, the teaching and absence of teachers, the use of teaching materials, the progress of teaching, the attendance and absence of students, the examination and performance evaluation of students, the self-study and extracurricular activities of students, the discipline and order of the school, the content of equipment such as library magazines, instruments, and specimens, hygiene facilities, military training, and sports are all examples of detailed inspections. The results of this inspection are very informative, and a report will be drafted and submitted to the Ministry for verification.

Memorial Service for the Wife of a World-Famous Scientist

To be Held in Shanghai This Month

The Shanghai French Association initiated a memorial service for Madame Marie Skłodowska Curie, the wife of the world-famous scientist. Mr. and Mrs. Weldon, the French Minister to China, and Mr. and Mrs. Weidento, the Polish Minister to China, were invited to co-host the event. The grand memorial ceremony is scheduled to be held at 5:45 PM on November 9th (Friday) in the auditorium of the French Association at No. 19 Huanlong Road. The order of lectures is as follows: (1) Mrs. Weidento, the Polish Minister, will speak on "Madame Curie's Posthumous Honors." (2) Dr. Lei Xie will speak on "A Summary of Madame Curie's Contributions in Science, Medicine, and Society." Dr. Lei is a disciple of Madame Curie and is currently a professor of radiology at Aurora University and the director of the radiology department at St. Mary's Hospital. The above two lectures have a lot of reference materials for the academic community, and it is heard that invitations have been sent to invite members of the Sino-Polish Cultural Association to participate.

Soochow Law School to Build a Law Library

Soochow Law School on Kunshan Road in this city has long been renowned at home and abroad for its research in comparative law. In recent years, it has vigorously innovated in academic subjects and implemented strict training to improve its level. Therefore, graduates have a wider outlet and are quite popular among all sectors of society. Among the graduates of this session, 21 are legal advisors in companies, banks, and various commercial organizations, 5 are judges, translators, and clerks in courts, 1 is studying in the UK, 3 are studying in the US, 8 are lecturers in law in universities and middle schools, and 5 are working in government agencies. Many of the jobs of these graduates are introduced by the school authorities. Recently, Fei Qing, a graduate of the 12th session of the school, won first place in the examination for government-funded students studying law in the United States this year. Also, Xu Fuji, a graduate of the 12th session of the school, won first place in the judicial officer examination conducted by the Nanjing Examination Yuan this time. It can be seen that graduates of the school often win first place in each examination. It is heard that the administrative authorities, in order to enrich the research materials on Chinese and Western law, have launched a fundraising campaign led by alumni Dong Kang, He Shizhen, Chen Tingrui, Jiang Yiping, Yang Yongqing, and Wu Jingxiong to build a large-scale law library. Famous figures of the Party and the State, Sun Ke, Wang Jingwei, Ju Zheng, Yu Youren, Dai Jitao, Cai Yuanpei, Wu Zhihui, Kong Xiangxi, and Wu Tiecheng, are listed as supporters, and fundraising has begun. The quota is set at 300,000 yuan. It is heard that the library is grand in scale, and its completion will make it the first law library in the East.

The Proactiveness of the Jinan University School of Commerce

The Jinan University School of Commerce in Zhenru was established very early and has produced many talented people. Many of the graduates of the school work in the banking and transportation industries in China, and it has an excellent reputation. Since Dong Xiujia took over last year, he has made great efforts to reorganize, pay attention to extracurricular activities, and increase students' interest in reading. Yesterday, the school held its second school affairs meeting at the China News Agency on Weihaiwei Road. Dong Xiujia, Zhang Sumin, Zhou Maofan, Wang Yong, and others attended the meeting. Dong Xiujia chaired the meeting. First, the chairman reported on the situation of the school this semester. Then, the following resolutions were made: (1) To establish a lecture series on modern economic issues and invite Yu Huan cheng, Chen Jintao, Yang Rumei, Lin Jinyu, Wu Shaozeng, Wu Wenwei, Cao Yunxiang, He Qingru, Li Gan, and He Bingxian to lecture on modern finance, modern accounting, modern railways, modern management, and modern foreign trade; (2) To hold a commercial problem speech contest; (3) To lead students to visit major commercial and transportation organizations in this city, etc.

East Asia Physical Education College Sports Meet Held in the Rain, Pan Yingchu Breaks National Record in Women's Javelin

Score: 28.05 Meters

Qian Hangsu and Others Participate in Exhibition

The East Asia Physical Education College located in Lu Jia Wan of this city is known far and wide for its excellent achievements. It goes without saying. The 7th of this month is the anniversary of the college's founding. Every year during this period, a sports meet is held to celebrate. It has been learned that the college will continue its usual practice of holding its 16th-anniversary sports meet over the past two days, focusing on track and field competitions. Therefore, the college's affiliated teachers will not be able to participate in the Shanghai Municipal Middle School Sports Meet, which begins on the 8th. As for ball games and group performances, they will be held at a later date. To increase the interest of general athletes, the college has invited those who scored points in the National Games, such as Qian Hangsu, Wang Huachang, Su Xiaoru, and Jia Lianren, to give exhibition performances. Only scores will be recorded, not rankings. Prizes will also be awarded to those with excellent scores. Yesterday, the weather was cloudy and the west wind howled. It was drizzling, and the ground was muddy, which significantly affected the results. The jumping events in the field events could not be held. However, the college students were well-trained, and the male and female athletes showed great spirit and were not at all intimidated. Reviewing the results, Qian Hangsu's 80-meter low hurdles time was 14.5 seconds, maintaining his national record. His 50-meter time was 7 seconds, very close to Ms. Zhang Jieqiong's national record of 6.9 seconds. Jia Lianren's 800-meter time was 2 minutes and 12 seconds. It is a pity that the track was loose and the turns were small. To achieve this result under those conditions was not easy. Female student Pan Yingchu is a rising star. Her javelin throw of 28.05 meters broke the national record. Xu Yuan also had a score of 26.98 meters. If she can put in more effort, her future prospects are unlimited. The Third Municipal Middle School Joint Sports Meet Opens Tomorrow

Venue: Jiaotong University Athletics Field, Duration: Three Days

More than 900 Athletes from Over 60 Schools Participate

The venue for the Third Municipal Middle School Joint Sports Meet, the athletic field of National Jiaotong University, is ready. The opening ceremony will be held tomorrow (the 8th) at 1:00 PM, followed by drills by each school, and then the sports events will begin. The meet will last for three days, with events starting at 1:00 PM each day. Athlete numbers were distributed yesterday. The following are the order of events and other information:

Route to the Venue

The venue for the meet is Jiaotong University in Xujiahui, but athletes and guests from all schools must enter the Jiaotong University stadium from Gaodun Road. Those attending can take the Xujiahui tram to the Fukaifeng Road intersection, walk west, enter Gaodun Road, and arrive at the gate of the Jiaotong University stadium. Do not enter from Xujiahui, so as not to interfere with the studies of Jiaotong University students.

Matters Requiring Attention by Each School

(1) All male and female track and field athletes and students participating in the meet's drills must attend the opening ceremony and must arrive at the venue by 12:30 PM to prepare. (2) The organizing committee will build reed sheds separately for the rest areas for male and female track athletes. The female athletes' rest area is in the north of the field, and the male athletes' rest area is in the west of the field. (3) The seating arrangement for each participating school will be arranged by the organizing committee. A seating chart will be drawn separately. It is hoped that each school will take its seats according to the designated location. (4) The seats for each school are all in the North, West, and South grandstand areas. It is hoped that you will bring your own reed mats to spread on the ground for the students to rest. (5) The seating chart and the lineup diagram for the march will be distributed to each school upon entry. (6) Photographs of athletes from Junyi, Guohua, Lehua, Chongde, the Affiliated Middle School of Aurora University, Hudong Junior High School, Zhengxing, Binhai, Wuling, and Minhua schools have not yet been submitted to the organizing committee. It is hoped that you will submit them to the Municipal No. 1 Sports Field on Daji Road before 5:00 PM on the 7th, so as not to have the athletes' numbers and other items withheld.

Spring and Autumn

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Four: A Cup of Water Shows the Difficulty of Seeking, a Poor Laborer Protects the Elderly, Ten Thousand Taels Can Be Obtained, Cunning Officials Unite in Groups

The old man was still holding that bowl in his hand, hesitating whether to raise his hand to scratch his head, and unknowingly raised the bowl above his head. Realizing it himself, he immediately lowered his hand. Zhichien also saw it and couldn't help but laugh. The old worker's pointed, thin face, covered with many wrinkles, also showed a layer of red. He took two steps back. At this time, Zhang Jiefu and Li Shilian were standing under the corridor eaves talking. They saw Zhichien go to the factory in the back alone, and they thought to themselves, what is there to see about a tiler working? He must be chasing after that girl to make contact. Let's see how he proceeds. Therefore, these two people frequently walked to the corridor eaves. Now they saw such a beardless old man, standing at the doorway, neither entering nor leaving. The situation was even more suspicious, so the two of them simply stayed nailed under the corridor eaves and didn't leave. Zhichien inside kept calling out, "Old Tan, come in, would I deceive you?" When the old man heard someone say the word "deceive," it seemed as if he was doubting other people's good intentions. That was unacceptable, so he smiled and walked in. Zhichien picked up the teapot on the table and nodded at him. The old worker was truly a bit overwhelmed by the favor. He held the tile bowl in both hands and came forward to receive it. As Zhichien poured into the bowl, he repeatedly said, "I don't deserve it." Zhichien poured more than half a bowl. He held the bowl, like a monkey holding a peach, holding the bowl in both hands, putting his mouth to it, raising his neck, and gulping it down, drinking the bowl of tea in one breath. He also drew out the sound, "Ah," to express his great admiration. On the table, there was also half a plate of biscuits, which Zhichien had left over. Thinking that it wouldn't be respectful to just have someone come and drink a bowl of tea, he picked up the half plate of biscuits and smiled at him, "Take these and try them." The old man stepped back and said "I dare not" twice. He half-extended his hand, pinched a piece of biscuit with three fingers, and put it between his front teeth, biting off a tiny bit. Then he clasped his hands and nodded slightly, saying, "That's it, that's it." (58)

When You Have No Money

— By Zigao

When you have no money, then you will surely discover the miraculous power of money:

Of course, you can still remember the scene when you were a wealthy man with money to spare, living in a foreign-style house, eating fish and meat, wearing silk and satin, and using a car for transportation. In the summer, you ran to Mogan Mountain to escape the heat, and in the cold weather, you hid in a room with a radiator, drinking wine and admiring the snow with your wife. When you had nothing to do, you played cards and had fun, listened to the radio, watched Peking opera, played jai alai, went to the dog track, the cinema, the nightclub... and all sorts of people who were neither relatives nor friends would greet you with smiling faces to flatter you. As long as you opened your mouth, anything could be done. The big shot had plenty of "money." However, once you encountered an adverse fate, leading to ruin and death, and you wandered alone, you would experience many of the hardships of having no money. You would lack clothing and food and have no place to live. In the summer, you could sleep on the cement ground for a night, but in the cold weather, you could only shiver next to a pile of garbage in an alley. You could listen to the radio on the street, which could be considered a small comfort in the midst of hardship. But you would never think of setting foot in those gold-consuming places like dance halls and jai alai courts again. At that time, even those useless people who were neither relatives nor friends and who used to greet you with smiling faces to flatter you would show you an icy face like a stranger. They might even scold you with a few words, "In a noisy city, no one asks about the poor; in the deep mountains, distant relatives are numerous for the rich." You would believe these two sentences without any doubt. Zhu Zhishan once wrote a couplet, "The rich are like swimming dragons, traveling all over the five mountains and four seas; the poor are like leftover tigers, scaring away all their relatives." That’s enough to describe the misery of having no money.

Yes, when you have no money, you will feel so many hardships. Even walking on the street, you will feel unusually constrained, as if your feet are chained, preventing you from moving. However, it also seems as if you are a runaway horse, and your four hooves want to leap forward. But you also think back to the scene when you had money!

Snippets

(Cold Jade)

Passing by Zhejiang Road, I saw a shop using live advertisements: a person dressed in white, wearing a mask and a tall hat, holding a large folding fan, promoting products. This was certainly a novel performance. Across the street, a foreign elderly couple was also watching intently. I wonder what they thought of this living "Wuchang" (a ghostly figure in Chinese folklore)?

Two Diligent Female Workers

— Ye Qibai

For the past six months, besides teaching many subjects during the day, I also ran a night school for the public in the evenings. The students in the night school were mostly girls, and these girls were mostly factory workers during the day.

I find their spirit of learning truly astonishing. So, they continuously sign up to enroll in the school, and I accept all who come, having already taken in over a hundred.

One day, before class started, and after I had prepared all my work, I casually looked around the classroom. As I was looking, two students happened to ask me about new characters. These two students were sisters. After I taught them, I started chatting with them casually. I asked, "Do you work during the day?" "Yes, we do." "Together?" "Yes." I then asked, "So, which factory do you work at?" "The Nanyang Tobacco Company." "That must be very inconvenient!" "Yes, we leave our home in Pudong in the morning and come back from the factory in the evening." "What about meals?" I asked further. "We just buy something to eat." "So, what time do you leave in the morning and return in the evening?" "We get up at five in the morning, wash our faces, and cross the river to the factory. We don't return until four or five in the afternoon." "That means you get home very late, and time is very rushed," I said. "Yes, when we get home, we grab our books and rush to the night class at six-thirty!" "What about dinner?" "We eat after the night class." "Oh! That must be very hard!" They didn't say anything, silently staring at the ground.

Later, I learned from other students about their difficult family situation, that they had an elderly grandmother and a disabled mother at home, and their father had died early. The livelihood of the two elderly people depended on the four hands of these two girls.

Who Will Win?

— Man Wu

Prayer

— Yangtze River

The solemn church was filled with a dense crowd of believers, men, women, the old, and the young, sitting together, so quiet that almost everyone could hear their own heartbeat. But in the front left corner sat only young women and older nuns; I soon learned that it was a specially arranged choir.

The choir sang as the main force, with many believers joining in. The tones were so harmonious, and the attitude was so solemn that even the piano did not break the harmonious unity. The piano is truly a strange thing! It can be played to accompany songs like "Drizzling Rain" and "Peach Blossom River," but it can also accompany this sacred hymn! —The piano itself has no sin; sin lies in those who use it.

"Jesus loves me, I love Jesus!" The church sang intensely and orderly, but outside the door, naughty children mischievously shouted, "Jesus loves me, I don't love Jesus!" The pastor's assistant came out to disperse them, and the solemn church lost some of its solemnity!

After that, it was the pastor's sermon, about the Heavenly Father and Christ, emphasizing that everyone should revere the Heavenly Father and Christ. But just revering isn't enough; you must also believe in Him, obey Him, and listen to all His words. Christ is always with us, so we must be careful in everything we do; attempting to deceive Him is impossible...

Finally: unanimous prayer from the entire congregation, each silently reciting their own prayer.

Short Story

The Matchmaker

— Yan Chonglou

(I)

Among Wei's friends, Ping often advised him to get married early. The reason was that Ping had a happy family, so she also hoped that her friends could have a happy family.

One day, Ping went to Wei's residence to find him and talked about this matter again:

"Wei, let me be your matchmaker. This is one of my cousins. She's two or three years younger than you and has received a considerable education at school," Ping said happily.

"Thank you for your kindness, but I want to focus all my energy on my career right now, so I don't want to get marri..." Wei hadn't finished speaking when Ping interrupted him:

"I know, you haven't met her in person, and you don't know what she looks like, so you don't want to. I'll bring her to the club tomorrow night for you to see. I'm definitely not an old-fashioned matchmaker, selling a cat in a bag, saying it's a white cat, but when you get it, it's a black cat!" Ping said, and without getting Wei's consent, she left smiling.

The next evening, Wei was playing games at the club when Ping indeed brought a girl, and as she walked in, she introduced her:

"This is my cousin," Ping said, then pointed at Wei and said to the girl she brought:

"This is Mr. Wei."

Wei asked them to sit down and chatted with them for a while, and then they got up to leave.

"Wei, I need to take my cousin home now. We'll see you in a few days," Ping said.

Wei didn't keep them and saw them to the door, watching them get into the car and leave.

(II)

A few days later, Wei met Ping again at the club; this time, Ping's cousin didn't come along.

"How was it? Were you satisfied with what you saw?" Ping asked Wei.

"What are you talking about?"

"The matchmaking I did for you!" Ping said coquettishly.

"Haha... I told you earlier that I want to focus on my career now, and I don't want to get married," Wei said solemnly.

"Really, you don't want to get married? Then don't you feel lonely!"

"Focusing on one's career can ward off the demon of loneliness."

"Actually, even married people feel lonely!" Ping's argument changed again, and she started talking about other things.

(III)

A long time passed, and once when Wei and Ping met, Wei casually asked about Ping's cousin. He learned that Ping's cousin had already gotten married. She married a wealthy man with a car, a Western-style house... She married him because he could satisfy her material desires. Ping also said that when she had initially talked to her cousin about Wei's situation, she wasn't very satisfied, although she did say that Wei was a promising young man. But in the end, she married a millionaire who was twice her age.

From this incident, Wei's conclusion was: "In this day and age, the most effective medium is still money!"

Records from the Fragrant Imperial Past

— Original by Princess Der Ling, translated by Qin Shouou

Her eyesight had never changed with her age, and at this moment, she was particularly attentive, so I thought she must have taken in all the scenery here in an instant! But she stood there for a long time, still motionless, as if these historical scenes had moved her thoughts like the Shanhaiguan Pass. The rest of us remained trembling and prostrate, even breathing extra carefully to avoid startling her. This frozen picture of one person standing solemnly and hundreds prostrating lasted for a full ten minutes. Later, she slowly moved her footsteps, but she stopped after walking only five or six steps; presumably, she intended to look at the scenery in another corner, and standing in the original place was inconvenient, so she wanted to move to a place where she could see more clearly.

Everyone kneeling remained motionless like clay sculptures or wooden carvings, the piles of colors as still as flowers inserted in a vase: because unless the Empress Dowager personally announced that we could stand up, no one, not even the Guangxu Emperor, dared to move on their own. And there was even less sound. At this time, only the Empress Dowager slowly paced around the hall with an extremely reserved and small gait. Her attitude seemed outwardly always very calm: but in my estimation, her hesitation at this time was actually a manifestation of inner panic. She herself might have wanted to find a place to rest quickly, or she might have wanted to lead everyone to inspect the place, or she might have wanted... In short, her thoughts must have been very confused, and she didn't know what to do for a moment, so she had to temporarily pace around the hall for a while!

In the past few days, she had been on the train and then carried in a phoenix carriage, so her entire life could be said to have been in a state of motion; now, returning to the stillness of the palace, she couldn't help but feel a little different! (168)

Commercial News

Finance

Gold Market on the Second Day of the Autumn Races Broke Through the Thousand Yuan Mark

—A Midday Result Showing a Further Increase of Six Yuan and Eight Jiao—

The gold market has been showing a mediocre situation for days. Yesterday was the second day of the Autumn Races. Traditionally, only the morning session is open for business. The market sentiment was exceptionally firm. Although the initial trading was relatively calm, once the buying spree started, the price surge was exceptionally strong. This is a typical trend during the race season. There is a saying about the "racetrack line," because with only half a day of trading, a sudden change is extremely difficult to stop. Yesterday, the market once broke through the 1,000 yuan mark. Initially, the overseas silver market showed London weakening and the U.S. remaining unchanged, with both exchange rates rising. London spot gold fell by three and a half pence. Off-market pre-trading retreated to 90 yuan and change. The Central Bank's official exchange rates were announced, with the U.S. rising by 0.0625. The customs gold rate fell by four li. The standard gold price retreated to 989 yuan and seven jiao. After a low opening in the morning, although it once fell back into the 90 yuan range, the market sentiment seemed firm. The buyers were particularly active. The HSBC bank's exchange rates were announced, with the U.S. rising by 0.0625, which was due to exchange rate factors and had little impact. The gold market hovered and remained stable. Later, the Central Bank's silver equalization tax rate was announced, remaining at 7.25 percent. Calculated with an exchange rate of one shilling and four pence and seventy-five points, the market was calm and unchanged at this time, hovering around one yuan. Afterwards, Chinese merchants showed a tendency to buy aggressively, and the domestic market was tight. With market sentiment already optimistic, the gold price gradually rose. Buyers became more and more numerous and bolder. Even with supply, it was difficult to compete. It broke through the 1,000 yuan mark. Banks took advantage of the high prices to sell, and prices fell back after reaching a high. However, because Yuan Mao, Yongfu, Yu, and others continued to buy gold bars, it was still possible to push prices higher, but it did not exceed the 1,000 yuan mark again. After this, more people took advantage of the high prices to sell. The midday close fell slightly, and the market was potentially tired and weak after the close. The trading during the half-day was still active, and the market turned bullish, but there was also a lack of special changes. The half-day market conditions are recorded below.

The morning opening was 990 yuan and two jiao, lower than the previous close by one yuan and two jiao. The Central Bank's exchange rates were announced, with the U.S. rising by 0.0625. The customs gold rate fell by four li. Shengda, Hengyu sold gold bars, and it retreated from 02 jiao to 90 yuan. Huixiang, Hengyu, Yongfeng, and Tongchun bought, rising to 07 jiao. Dachang, Xiangfu, Yu, Hengyu came to sell, falling to 89 yuan and a half. At this time, banks were trading with each other. Yinghui, Huixiang, Dingkang, Fuxing, Yonglai bought. HSBC's exchange rates were announced, and the market sentiment was still good, gradually rising to 91 yuan and seven jiao. Zhaofeng, Chang Dingkang, Fuyu sold, and it fell to 90 yuan. At this time, it was maintained because Hengyu, Fuxing, and Yongli continued to buy. The Central Bank's silver equalization tax rate remained unchanged. At this time, it hovered around one yuan. After entering, the December shilling 9375 was difficult to settle. Fuan, Tongtai, Changda, Decheng, Dakang, and others went up to 2 yuan and four jiao. Fuxing, Yong, Zhaofeng, Chang, Shunli, Dafa, Yong, although they sold to 1 yuan and seven jiao, but Yifeng, Yongyu, Qingyong, Zhengchang, Fuxing, Yong, Fuyu, Yuanmao, Yong, Yuansheng, Yong, Yuanchun, Hengxingyuan, etc. rushed to buy gold bars, gradually rising to 7 yuan and nine jiao. Although Yicheng and Dingkang had supply, they only struggled a little. After that, Zhentai and Dafa Yong sold, retreating to 7 yuan and one jiao, but the buying was still strong. Yuanmao, Yongfu, Yu, Hengxingyuan, Fuxing, Yong, etc. bought again, breaking through the 1,000 yuan mark, rising to 1,001 yuan and a half. Wanxing, Dafa Yong, Qianchang, Xiang, Qingyu, Fuchang, Yuan Yi, etc. sold, and the Chinese-Belgian Bank sold January shillings at 8125, gradually falling to 997 yuan. Yuanmao Yong bought fiercely. Yifeng Yong, Yuanchang Yong, Chunyuan Yong, Fuyu also bought, rising back to 9 yuan and six jiao. Qianchang Xiang, Wanxing, Dingkang sold down, falling to 8 yuan. The midday close was 998 yuan. After the close, Fuxing Yong, Yicheng, Wanxing, Shunli, and others continued to supply, and finally fell to 7 yuan. The highest price during the half-day was 1,001 yuan and a half, and the lowest price was 989 yuan and a half, a difference of 12 yuan. As a result, it rose again by 6 yuan and 6 jiao compared to the previous close.

The closing price was announced by the Central Bank's standard gold price at 989 yuan and seven jiao. In terms of the closing price, the standard gold price was raised again by 8 yuan, less than the previous close by more than 8 yuan. Halved Transportation Fee Approved for Hubei Silk Cocoons

Mianyang and other counties in Hubei Province are rich in yellow and white silk cocoons. In recent years, due to the drastic decline in sales of foreign silk, the decline of the silk industry in Hubei Province is the same as in Jiangsu and Zhejiang. Silk merchants in Hubei jointly submitted a request to the Ministry of Industry, requesting that the transportation fee for silk cocoons from Hubei Province, when transported by China Merchants Steam Navigation Company ships, be reduced by half the original price, following the example of silk cocoon transportation in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, in order to provide relief. According to the Hubei silk merchants in Shanghai, the Ministry of Industry has approved the request and instructed the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to handle the matter accordingly.

Free Talk

The Literati and Poverty

— Zhou Benzhai

It seems that there has always been some kind of connection between literati and poverty. In reality, who is not poor? How can the poverty of literati compare to the poverty of non-literati? However, literati take poverty as a "common topic," as if only literati are poor, and the poverty of non-literati does not count for anything.

When literati talk about poverty, on the one hand, they are expressing their elegance, and on the other hand, they believe that poverty is related to literature. The so-called "poverty leads to craftsmanship," even if it is not the primary motivation, it is at least a driving force. When one is poor, one's writing becomes "craftful," which is remarkable. However, non-literati cannot talk about these things. It is precisely because they are poor that they are called vulgar people by the so-called elegant people. It is precisely because they are poor that they are not only unable to become literati, but also isolated by literature, losing the tool for conveying emotions to each other. It is precisely because they are poor that they form this special group of literati. Moreover, even poverty has become a tool for literati to claim and flaunt themselves, and their poverty is rejected outside the circle, counting for nothing.

The poverty of literati must be different from the poverty of non-literati.

Then, the poverty of non-literati is the poverty of life; the poverty of literati is the poverty of circumstances. Literati are the elite among intellectuals. Intellectuals are scholars. Scholars are those who seek officialdom, who want to "learn well and then become officials." Not becoming an official means not being recognized; not being recognized means being poor. The ancients often used the words "poverty" and "success" in contrast, which is the meaning of this. As Mencius said: "In poverty, do not lose righteousness; in success, do not depart from the way." He also said: "When poor, cultivate your own moral character; when successful, benefit all under heaven." If poverty refers to the poverty of life, how can one "cultivate one's own moral character"? Literati have always followed this meaning.

Due to the difference between poverty and success, literature also presents different perspectives. The literature of the successful is celebratory literature. The literature of the poor is lament literature. Ouyang Xiu clearly explained this division in his "Preface to the Poetry Collection of Mei Shengyu": "I have heard the world say that poets are rarely successful and mostly poor. Is this really the case? The poems that are passed down in the world mostly come from the words of poor people in ancient times. All scholars who have their talents and cannot apply them to the world mostly like to indulge themselves outside the mountains and rivers, seeing the forms and categories of insects, fish, grass, trees, wind, clouds, birds, and beasts, often exploring their strangeness, with the depression of worries, thoughts, and anger inside. Their poems arise from resentment and satire, expressing the laments of exiled officials and widowed women, and writing the unspeakable feelings of people. The poorer they are, the more craftful they become. Therefore, it is not that poetry can impoverish people, but rather that it is after being impoverished that they become craftful. My friend Mei Shengyu, as a young man, was appointed as a historian through family privilege, and was repeatedly suppressed by officials in the imperial examinations, struggling in the states and counties for more than ten years. At the age of fifty, he was still following appointment letters, serving as an assistant to others, suppressing his accumulated talents and not being able to show them in his career... However, regardless of the wise or the foolish, those who talk about poetry must seek it from Shengyu. Shengyu himself also takes pleasure in poetry and expresses it because of his frustrations. Therefore, his lifelong works are mostly poetry. The world already knows this, but no one has recommended him to the court... If he were fortunate enough to be used in the court, writing odes and hymns to sing the praises of the great Song dynasty's merits and virtues, recommending them to the Qing Temple, and following the authors of odes in the Shang, Zhou, and Lu dynasties, wouldn't that be great! Why should he be allowed to grow old without success, and write poems of the poor, only expressing the words of insects, fish, things, melancholy, and lamentation? The world only likes his craftsmanship, not knowing that his poverty has been long-lasting and he is about to grow old. It is a pity!" Here, what is said that "poetry cannot impoverish people" is very true. Not only can poetry not impoverish people, but on the contrary, it can make people not poor and successful. Poetry and writing were originally tools for scholars to become officials. If the tool is effective, then one succeeds and writes celebratory literature. This is what it means to "be fortunate enough to be used in the court, writing odes and hymns to sing the praises of ××'s merits and virtues, recommending them to the Qing Temple, and following the authors of odes in the Shang, Zhou, and Lu dynasties," wouldn't that be great! If the tool is ineffective, then one is poor and writes lament literature. This is what it means to "express the words of insects, fish, things, melancholy, and lamentation," which is a pity!

But if the so-called "poverty leads to craftsmanship," "the poorer one is, the more craftful one becomes," there is a distinction to be made. First of all, this poverty refers to the poverty of circumstances, not the poverty of life. The content of poverty determines the content of "craftsmanship." Secondly, even if the poverty of circumstances affects the poverty of life, this is only in relation to success and is simply poverty. Therefore, one still cannot feel the true experience of poverty in life and cannot write the true reality of poverty in life. If we talk about "craftsmanship," it is the "craftsmanship" of lament, the so-called "craftful in sorrow and good at illness."

On the Banks of the Red River

— Liubing

Near that distant equator, lies quietly Bandung, known as the "Switzerland of the East." There, tropical coconut trees thrive beneath the deep blue sky, and clumps of white clouds drift suspended from the coconut leaves. The people who live there all carry weary hearts and faces tanned by the sun. Bandung is beautiful, and the people in Bandung all have beautiful hearts. Not far from Bandung, there is an even more beautiful river that winds through Java, with coconut trees forming riverbanks on both sides. Monkeys leap and sing in the unknown vines. This is the serene Red River.

Three years ago, I wandered to the banks of the Red River as if in a dream. Once my traveler's heart, petrified by the city, came into contact with this beautiful nature, it unconsciously became attached. In the evening, I liked to go to the banks of the Red River alone, holding my mandolin, sitting under the tall coconut trees, facing the crescent moon, facing the quiet river, playing my favorite tunes, and humming unfamiliar Malay melodies.

One evening, as I was singing a Malay tune, an elderly Malay man came. He said in a low voice:

"Wah! The moon is really good tonight!" (Malay people call young men "wah")

"Hmm! Do you also love this place, old man?" I started talking to him in Malay.

"I know you love this place. I see you sitting here every night, and I hear your singing."

"Yes! Look, how quiet the sky is here, how beautiful the river is!"

"Wah! Do you say the river is beautiful! It is red!"

"But the river is not red at all!" I said, looking at it.

"Hehe! This river was once stained with the blood of you Chinese!" he shouted in a trembling voice.

"The blood of the Chinese?"

"Yes! The blood of the Chinese has dyed this river red!" He sat down beside me, lowering his head. After a while, he slowly raised his head, his eyes filled with grief and indignation, and said in a low voice: "Wah! Do you know why this river is called the Red River? There is a moving story here. It was a long time ago, your Chinese ancestors came to Java to trade with our ancestors. Then, your ancestors planted fields and built houses in Java, and lived a peaceful life with our ancestors.

"But, wah! One day, many white people suddenly came, the white people who now rule this place, they wanted your ancestors' land, they wanted your ancestors' houses. But they were afraid of the Chinese emperor, so they didn't dare to act. Later, I heard that they went to see your Chinese emperor, saying that the Chinese were bullying them, and asking the emperor to severely punish them, ha! What did your emperor say? He said that your ancestors were people outside the pale of civilization and had nothing to do with the Celestial Empire. So the white people came back. They had guns and cannons, and your ancestors were people forgotten by their motherland, and were brutally killed by the white people. The Chinese retreated, all the way to the riverbank, and could not retreat any further, and were killed one by one by those vicious white people, and the corpses were thrown into the river, and the river was stained with the blood of the Chinese, and turned red, and this river was called the Red River!"

"Wah! Now the river water has long been clear, but the Chinese are still forgotten by their homeland!"

After saying this, the old man walked away falteringly. I looked at his departing figure, looked at the river, and the river turned red before my eyes. I hurriedly closed my eyes and ran back. The old man's words were deeply imprinted on my heart:

Chinese people forgotten by their motherland!

Wonton Noodle Carrier

— TK

Parting

— Yanfu

With a tense and melancholic heart, I went to Hong Kong with Zi.

This trip to Hong Kong was because I was waiting for a ship to return to Shanghai. Hong Kong is a place I often visit. Every summer vacation, I would travel back and forth to my hometown, always leaving hurried footprints on this bustling island with a few classmates; but this time was special. The person who came with me was not a classmate returning to Shanghai, but Zi, who came to see me off.

Seeing her reluctant expression, how could I not be melancholic? The night before my departure, I told her the news that I was returning to Shanghai. She immediately cried, sobbing on the pillow, tightly holding my hand, as if she had thousands of words to tell me, but couldn't say a word. It wasn't until I ran out to the hall to say goodbye to her family that she wiped away her tears and saw me home from the late night.

We arrived in Hong Kong the day before the ship sailed because we wanted to take a look at the cabins in advance. That day, we especially crossed the sea from Hong Kong to Kowloon. On the ferry, I saw the huge Russian Empress in the distance, and couldn't help but shed tears.

After spending the night in Hong Kong, I disembarked the next morning. The cabin was crowded with passengers and coolies. I found a berth, put my luggage away, and ran to the deck with Zi. In order to dispel her sadness of parting, I often told her about my past travels, and sometimes deliberately asked her other questions, but she always remained silent.

"Zi, look, the color of the sea is really beautiful. Do you see that sailboat far away?" I asked her deliberately again.

There was no reply. Looking at her, her eyes were red and filled with tears.

We were both silent, and memories of the summer vacation flooded my mind. I remembered the cool breeze on Yuexiu Mountain at dawn, and the golden water in Lychee Bay at dusk.

The time for the ship to sail arrived, and the bell warning the send-off had already rung. I led her out of the cabin. When we reached the gangway, she suddenly tightly held my hand:

"I wish you—a—smooth—voyage—"

Her throat choked up, her tears flowed down again, and my eyes couldn't help but burst into a few hot tears. Wiping her eyes, she said again:

"Come back quickly as soon as summer vacation starts next year"!

Her trembling voice came from a helpless mood. I nodded and helped her onto the gangway. When tears flowed down again, the gangway was lowered by the workers.

The ship was moving slowly. I stood on the deck, waving my handkerchief to her, and tears flowed down even more uncontrollably. Wiping my eyes with the waving handkerchief, I raised it again and waved it so enthusiastically. At this moment, a burst of music from the music room spread out as the ship sailed, every sound piercing my heart!

Scenery of Beiping (One-Act Comedy) (V)

— Xu Jie

(Zhang Dejuan enters)

Han: Miss Zhang, I've been thinking about you so much, you've finally come! Do you know how much I love you? (Moves closer)

Zhang: Who are you?

Han: I love you, do you know that? (Hugs her) Miss Zhang! You're so lovely, this is the first time in my life I've seen someone like you! My father always said my mother was lovely, and my mother was beautiful, but they're not even one ten-thousandth as lovely as you!

Zhang: You... you... you.

Han: (Kisses her) I love you, your lips are so tender! (Kiss) My dear, you're so lovely!

Zhang: Oh! Your arms are so strong! You... you're also really lovely!

Bu: (Enters) Old Han!

Han: (Surprised)...

Han: I was beside myself, Miss Zhang! We're using a ploy today. I think you and Bu should continue to love each other!

Zhang: A ploy?

Han: We originally wanted him to come and comfort you when I forced myself on you, but who knew I'd be beside myself! Old Bu! I'm really sorry! But, you two should still love each other in the future!

Zhang: Mr. Han, it's strange, I was really drawn to you! I'll love you forever now!

Han: Miss Zhang! But I'm not as rich as this fellow here! Old Bu loves you very much, don't make me wrong my friend!

Zhang: But I only love you!

Bu: Old Han! Love is like this, alright, you two be lovers!

Liu: Old Han! What do we do? (Enters)

Han: Arms can only be used for love.

Liu: Toppling the shopkeeper requires wisdom.

Han: I believe it now!

Bu: I believe it too!

Liu: (Shouts) Shopkeeper! Shopkeeper!

(Shopkeeper enters)

Liu: Go and invite your shopkeeper here!

Shopkeeper: Yes! (Exits)

Han: Why did you call him here?

Liu: Naturally there's something to be done, you see my wisdom is inexhaustible.

Bu: What?

(The shopkeeper enters)

Liu: Shopkeeper Wang! We're not selling the shop board.

Shopkeeper: Hmm... it's good not to sell, but return the two dollars to me.

Liu: (Holding two dollars, ringing.) Shopkeeper Wang! You're truly a chivalrous person! Look, this is Miss Zhang, this is Shopkeeper Wang, the most generous Shopkeeper Wang!

Zhang Han: (Affectionately)

Bu: Shopkeeper Wang, the two of them are getting married here today, is that alright?

Shopkeeper: Alright! Alright!

Liu: (Writes two pieces of paper and hands them to the shopkeeper) These are invitations, please come and drink at the wedding today.

Shopkeeper: I'll definitely come to congratulate, I'll definitely come to congratulate. (Wants to leave.)

Liu: Send a small gift, I'm embarrassed!

Shopkeeper: I don't have any money!

Liu: Let's consider those two dollars as a gift!

Shopkeeper: Hmm... is the money still with you?

Liu: Alright? Old Bu, receive the two dollars from Shopkeeper Wang as a gift!

(Liu hands the money to Bu) Shopkeeper Wang, then come and drink wedding wine tonight!

Shopkeeper: I'll definitely come, I'll definitely come. (Wants to leave.)

Liu: Ah! That's right! The wedding wine hasn't been prepared yet, Shopkeeper, go and prepare it for me!

Shopkeeper: Where's the money?

Liu: You're a chivalrous person, I'll definitely return it to you in the future.

Shopkeeper: I don't have any money either.

Liu: Then ah! Then just order two more meals!

Shopkeeper: Hmm... but I'll write it in your debt!

Liu: Of course! No need to say that.

(Shopkeeper leaves)

Liu: Shopkeeper Wang, come and drink wedding wine tonight!

Shopkeeper: Definitely, definitely.

Liu: (To Bu) How is it? Ah! There's more! (Shouts) Shopkeeper, shopkeeper!

(Shopkeeper enters)

Liu: Bring five wine cups when it's time to eat! We'll drink wine tonight.

Shopkeeper: Yes.

— Curtain —

(Note) "Drum beater" refers to a person in Beiping who buys old goods, named for calling out purchases by beating a drum.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

On Leisurely Living

— Ge Bai

Leisure is a virtue, that gentle gentlemanly demeanor is the unique national characteristic of us Chinese.

In the morning, go to a teahouse with a birdcage, for lunch, go to a storytelling house to chew melon seeds and spiced beans, come back and take a turn at Daoxiangcun or Laoda Fang, carrying back triangular, rectangular, large and small packages of tea snacks and candies, and for dinner, even better, have three cups of sorghum liquor, and then in an orderly manner, enjoy the pleasure under the lamp with your wife and children, eat sesame nougat, talk about the turtles being released in the City God Temple, within a room, joy and harmony, lying on the bed, you won’t have nightmares about a big fire burning next door, and a night passes without a word, straight until the next morning, when the red sun fills the window again.

Firstly, you were indeed born into the right womb, born as a Chinese person, and secondly, your ancestors accumulated virtue, whether they created sins or shed sweat, it is always a blessing for their children and grandchildren, as long as you kowtow and offer sacrifices in a proper manner during the four seasons and eight festivals, your conscience will be clear, and you will be a filial son and obedient citizen.

If you have a moment of leisure, play eight rounds of mahjong, or have a tea gathering, we can't say it's wild gambling, it's hard to live a lifetime, why get up at dawn? If you smoke opium, you can both protect your ancestral property and reduce internal heat, all beauty is available, and nothing is lacking, the way of leisure ends here!

Observe in a small room, the bean-sized lamp dimly lit, raising your leg like that, tilting your head, puffing smoke, looking at each other with one eye, a mouthful of strong tea and a mouthful of smoke, not to mention the loss of the Northeast, which is far away, even if the January 28th Incident’s gunfire is everywhere, it's just a matter of going up to the third floor to watch the big fire burning in Zhabei from afar.

Other small matters, if it rains when you go out, don't rush around, you must know that it's better to get your clothes wet than to disrupt your pace; when calling a rickshaw, don't say "a dime," but say "two hundred and forty cash," because big (foreign) and small (coins) are different, and when having a bowl of porridge, think about where it came from. During the Mid-Autumn Festival, admire the moon by climbing onto the drying platform and pacing back and forth, and in October, eat crabs and write poetry with a bottle of chrysanthemum wine. On New Year's Eve, burn a vigil candle, and on New Year's Day, personally light the incense for the heavens.

Beside the opium couch, teach your children to read, hoping they will surpass you!

Reflections on the Opening of the New Cambridge Library

— Lie Huo

According to reports, the Cambridge University in England just opened a new library, with shelf space for 43 miles of books, containing 1.5 million volumes. A generous donation was made by the American oil tycoon. After reading this, I was filled with lament. I am working in a university in China, which proudly bears the title of "National." The poverty of its book collection is so depressing that it makes one breathless. Several times I went to borrow some ordinary books, checking the catalog over and over again, and nineteen times out of twenty I was disappointed. A friend from a private university, with great hope, came to borrow books for a specialized topic, but I took him there and he found nothing.

I believe, and I am even more certain, that this is not a miracle. The poverty of book collections in Chinese universities is probably the general situation.

Perhaps some people will come out and explain: "China is a poor country, and the history of its libraries is very short, so of course it cannot compare with foreign countries; in another thirty or fifty years, it will no longer be as poor as it is now." But how can this convince people? China's history is longer than that of foreign countries, and according to the law of "accumulation," we should be stronger than foreign countries. If this continues, it will be the same even after another thirty or fifty years, I dare to say.

What is the problem? It is that the general school funding is allocated so improperly, with administrative expenses occupying the highest peak of the curve on the statistical paper, while construction expenses are truly minimal, and the purchase of books naturally has to be put aside. Moreover, schools are often bureaucratic, and those in charge are afflicted with the "five-day magistrate of the capital" mentality, counting each day as it comes, and no one is willing to work hard for the future of the school. What construction is there to talk about? Just getting by is enough.

Speaking of this, I am even more reminded of the wealthy people in China who possess vast fortunes, but are also extremely stingy, only seeking enjoyment in their own lives, and few are willing to take out money to run cultural undertakings. There is no one like Rockefeller who donates 250,000 pounds at a time. The ×× Library was destroyed in the January 28th Incident, and two years later it still had to rely on donations from Germany to be restored. Having such a relatively good library to support the scene is still something that is barely satisfactory.

I wonder what the people of the country will think after reading the above news? And the decline of Chinese cultural standards is probably related to this!

Mother

— Chen Liang

Every time I return home, I see that my mother's hair is thinner each time, mixed with gray in the withered and scorched hair, and the bun has been eroded smaller by the passing years.

Mother was born in the countryside, she cut grass for sheep, herded cattle, and carried firewood on the shoulder pole to the market when she was young. It is said that at that time, a chicken egg was only three copper coins, and a sesame cake was a big piece for one copper coin, but my mother rarely got to taste them. Later, she came to Shanghai and worked with my father in the workshop, working until midnight, and going to sleep hungry. Now, she still has to take care of the housework, and in the morning, she takes a scale and a basket to the vegetable market, and she will buy back the things we like to eat, like pumpkins and taro. When I am not at home, she stubbornly sets aside a little of what the family has for me—even if it's moldy, she still has to keep it.

I will never forget that when I am working outside, I always paste my mother's face on my eyelids, looking at it in a daze in my mind, that kind and gentle smile, the wide and faint eyebrows on her brown-yellow face, the ordinary nose, and the years of trachoma sufferer, her eyes always surrounded by tears, her mouth is a mouth that will not say an angry word, her gentle voice can make a disobedient and unruly son kneel down and repent. In my dreams in a foreign land, I often seem to hear my mother calling my name faintly. But! When I open my eyes, where is my mother? At home, her gentle voice and kind face are carried on my journey of life, like a radio, it provokes thoughts and comforts the sorrow of separation.

It seems like two sharp nails were hammered into my mother's life. When she recalls the untimely deaths of my two older brothers, it will stir up some old pain.

"Having raised you this big, you can talk, laugh, and jump. When you were little and had some illnesses, it made me like a headless fly. I don't expect you to get rich or get promoted, but don't forget the suffering of your mother raising you." Whenever my younger brother and I are playing and jumping in front of my mother, she will repeat these words.

When I'm outside, I often think about bringing something back for my mother to eat, but, there's nothing! Fruits are cooling, and my mother has had a cold stomach for years. Snacks are something she has always rejected, but she makes an exception for chestnuts, she loves the charred aroma of chestnuts. But she doesn't want me to buy them often, "It's hard to earn money, save what you can." I firmly remember these words and write them in thick ink in my notebook, adding some kind gestures, wrapped in a clean handkerchief, great maternal love is always deeply hidden in the son's heart, what can I boast about to the world? I have no affinity for inheritance, what I will receive is—

Mother's great love.

Shanghai's First Nursery Has Closed

— Bu Bai

In our large country of China, we lag behind in everything, but our culture was the first to develop, so we consider foreigners as barbarians and are arrogant. However, since the Opium War (strictly speaking, it should be after the Boxer Rebellion), this self-respecting mentality was shattered by the material civilization of the great powers! So we blindly imitate foreigners, taking foreigners as our guide, echoing what others say, it is truly ridiculous.

I say, imitating foreigners is not bad in itself, but if we imitate blindly and have no creativity of our own, then that kind of imitation is too meaningless, isn't it? Our imitation should be creative.

Recently, on the cultural scene, due to the large number of "foreign" theories imported from abroad, people have seized on a theory and implemented it regardless of the Chinese environment.

Page 18

However, because they have not considered that theory is related to the environment, they often shatter their beautiful ideals and are left with a painful face, not knowing what to do!

In the past, there was a debate about nurseries. Those who argued that nurseries could exist in China often used the nurseries in the Soviet Union as an analogy to explain the reasons why they could exist, which is quite ridiculous. You must know that the reason why nurseries can be "truly" implemented in the Soviet Union is that the political system in the Soviet Union is fundamentally different from that in China. As for the reasons why nurseries can exist in capitalist countries (of course, this existence is different from that in the Soviet Union), it is because nurseries are fundamentally one of the social policies of capitalism. Looking back at our China, has capitalism developed as much as in England and America?

Therefore, the principle of nurseries is correct, but to implement it in China, one must consider the Chinese environment. I once talked to a steel factory worker who was distressed about having children. I enthusiastically said to him, "Why not send them to a nursery?" When he learned that the monthly boarding fee for nurseries was eight yuan, he stuck out his tongue and said, "I dont even earn twenty yuan a month, how can I use eight yuan to send one child to a nursery?" So he told me that his children are boarded in the countryside, and only two yuan a month is enough for boarding fees!

If China wants to run nurseries, it must reduce the boarding fees to two yuan, but is that possible in reality? My answer is so decisive: "Impossible!" You see, the closure of the First Nursery, although it does not explicitly state that it is because of economic reasons, is actually because they are going to "try out" a "small-scale" one in the future, which shows that they are economically strapped! So, even with an eight-yuan boarding fee, they still feel strapped!

Finally, I must solemnly declare: I do not oppose the principle of nurseries at all, but I sincerely hope that those who run nurseries, or those who are enthusiastic about nurseries, should not abuse foreign theories (Soviet or even British and American) and not consider the current Chinese environment at all.

Journey

— Yong Bo

Night.

The night shrouded the hazy mountains and fields, and a strange wind howled: a will-o'-the-wisp floated among the desolate tombs, adorning this gloomy world.

I swung my exhausted limbs, looked around, and then tremblingly sat down on the roadside signpost. A moment of rest is hard-won.

I silently murmured in loneliness: This long journey, burdened with the scars of thorns. — The scars have been accumulated for a long time!

Under the shining of the stars, I examined the blood stains on my chest and shoulders, but my heart suddenly felt a sharp pain. The thorns are so sharp! So keen! Moreover, there are poisonous snakes lurking on both sides, jackals hiding, and man-eating tigers and leopards spying. — Dangerous! Truly dangerous! This journey that has been walked.

But, isn't the road ahead the same? The thorns are higher and denser, denser and sharper, and there are still poisonous snakes, jackals, tigers, and leopards hiding on both sides; where will I go with my scarred and broken body?

Wandering in the middle, I can only wait quietly for death to come; retreating to the original road, why did I bother to endure this pain and suffering in the first place? Now the only way out is to move forward, forward, constantly forward!

I looked around and silently murmured in loneliness:

— Night will surely pass; dawn will surely be born.

All the will-o'-the-wisps suddenly disappeared.

Huaxing (1260) 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM

Song of Everlasting Regret (Continued) by Bai Juyi

The world spun, the dragon chariot turned back, hesitating to leave.

Under the Mawei Slope, in the soil, the jade face was gone, only a burial place remained.

The emperor and his ministers looked at each other, their clothes soaked with tears.

Looking east towards the capital, they let the horses return.

Returning, the pools and gardens were all as before, the lotus of Taiye and the willows of Weiyang.

The lotus resembled her face, the willows her eyebrows, how could they not weep at this?

Spring breeze, peach blossoms, and plum blossoms bloomed; autumn rain, wutong leaves fell.

In the West Palace and South Palace, autumn grass grew luxuriantly, fallen leaves filled the steps, un-swept.

The disciples of the pear garden had new white hair, the eunuchs of the pepper chamber and the beautiful concubines grew old.

In the evening palace, the fireflies flickered quietly; the solitary lamp was trimmed to its end, yet sleep would not come.

Slowly, the bells and drums began the long night; the glistening Milky Way was about to dawn.

The mandarin duck tiles were cold, heavy with frost; in the emerald quilt, who was there to share it with?

Life and death were separated by many years; the souls would not come into dreams.
